#### City neighborhoods

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: City neighborhoods")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Sacramento_%2C_California_%2833994662274%29.jpg/250px-Sacramento_%2C_California_%2833994662274%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sacramento_,_California_(33994662274).jpg)

[Downtown Sacramento](/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento") is the home of numerous corporate regional headquarters.

The city used to group neighborhoods into four areas. As of 2011, the groupings were:

* Area One: [Alkali Flat](/wiki/Alkali_Flat_Historic_District "Alkali Flat Historic District"), [Boulevard Park](/wiki/Boulevard_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Boulevard Park, Sacramento, California"), Campus Commons, [Sacramento State](/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento "California State University, Sacramento"), Dos Rios Triangle, Downtown, East Sacramento, Mansion Flats, Marshall School, [Midtown](/wiki/Midtown_Sacramento "Midtown Sacramento"), [New Era Park](/wiki/New_Era_Park,_Sacramento,_California "New Era Park, Sacramento, California"), McKinley Village, [Newton Booth](#Newton_Booth_Historic_District), [Old Sacramento](/wiki/Old_Sacramento_State_Historic_Park "Old Sacramento State Historic Park"), [Poverty Ridge](#Poverty_Ridge_Historic_District), Richards, Richmond Grove, River Park, Elmhurst, Sierra Oaks, [Southside Park](/wiki/Southside_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Southside Park, Sacramento, California").[[36]](#cite_note-37)
* Area Two: Airport, Carleton Tract, Freeport Manor, Golf Course Terrace, [Greenhaven](/wiki/Pocket-Greenhaven,_Sacramento,_California "Pocket-Greenhaven, Sacramento, California") Hollywood Park, [Land Park](/wiki/Land_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Land Park, Sacramento, California"), Little Pocket, Mangan Park, [Meadowview](/wiki/Meadowview,_Sacramento,_California "Meadowview, Sacramento, California"), Parkway, [Pocket](/wiki/Pocket-Greenhaven,_Sacramento,_California "Pocket-Greenhaven, Sacramento, California"), [Sacramento City College](/wiki/Sacramento_City_College "Sacramento City College"), [South Land Park](/wiki/Land_Park,_Sacramento,_California#South_Land_Park "Land Park, Sacramento, California"), Valley Hi / North Laguna, Z'Berg Park.[[37]](#cite_note-38)
* Area Three: Alhambra Triangle, Avondale, Brentwood, Carleton Tract, [Colonial Heights](/wiki/Colonial_Heights,_Sacramento,_California "Colonial Heights, Sacramento, California"), Colonial Manor, [Curtis Park](/wiki/Curtis_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Curtis Park, Sacramento, California"), [Elmhurst](/wiki/Elmhurst,_Sacramento,_California "Elmhurst, Sacramento, California"), Fairgrounds, [Florin](/wiki/Florin,_California "Florin, California"), Fruitridge Manor, Glen Elder, Glenbrook, Granite Regional Park, Industrial Park, Lawrence Park, Med Center, North City Farms, [Oak Park](/wiki/Oak_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Oak Park, Sacramento, California"), [Packard Bell](/wiki/Packard_Bell "Packard Bell"), South City Farms, [Southeast Village](/wiki/Southeast_Village "Southeast Village"), [Tahoe Park](/wiki/Tahoe_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Tahoe Park, Sacramento, California"), [Tahoe Park East](/wiki/Tahoe_Park,_Sacramento,_California#Tahoe_Park_East "Tahoe Park, Sacramento, California"), [Tahoe Park South](/wiki/Tahoe_Park_South "Tahoe Park South"), Tallac Village, Vintage Park, Churchill Downs, and Woodbine.[[38]](#cite_note-39)
* Area Four: [Ben Ali](/wiki/Ben_Ali,_Sacramento,_California "Ben Ali, Sacramento, California"), [Del Paso Heights](/wiki/Del_Paso_Heights,_Sacramento,_California "Del Paso Heights, Sacramento, California"), Gardenland, Hagginwood, McClellan Heights West, [Natomas](/wiki/Natomas,_Sacramento,_California "Natomas, Sacramento, California") (north, south, west), [North Sacramento](/wiki/North_Sacramento "North Sacramento"), Northgate, [Robla](/wiki/Robla,_Sacramento,_California "Robla, Sacramento, California"), Swanston Estates, Terrace Manor, [Valley View Acres](/wiki/Valley_View_Acres,_Sacramento,_California "Valley View Acres, Sacramento, California"), and Woodlake.[[39]](#cite_note-40)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Sacramento_Riverfront.jpg/250px-Sacramento_Riverfront.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sacramento_Riverfront.jpg)

[Old Sacramento](/wiki/Old_Sacramento "Old Sacramento") and [Downtown](/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento") are seen from the [Sacramento River](/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River").

Other neighborhoods in the city include Cal Expo, Capital Avenue, College/Glen, Creekside, Elder Creek, Erikson Industrial Park, Gateway Center, Gateway West, Glenwood Meadows, Hansen Park, Heritage Park, Johnson Business Park, Johnson Heights, Metro Center, Natomas Corporate Center, Natomas Creek, Natomas Crossing, Natomas Park, Newton Booth, Noralto, Northpointe, Norwood, Oak Knoll, Old North Sacramento, Parker Homes, Point West, Raley Industrial Park, Regency Park, Richardson Village, Richmond Grove, Sierra Oaks, Sports Complex, Strawberry Manor, Sundance Lake, Upper Land Park, Village 5, Village 7, Village 12, Village 14, Village Green, West Del Paso Heights, Westlake, Willowcreek, Wills Acres, Winn Park, and Youngs Heights.[[40]](#cite_note-41)

#### Notable areas

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Notable areas")]

##### Capitol Mall

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Capitol Mall")]

Capitol Mall connects West Sacramento and Downtown Sacramento. Some notable landmarks on this road include the Tower Bridge, Old Sacramento, and the California State Capitol Building. Capitol Mall is considered to be the business district of the city. Skyscrapers such as the [Wells Fargo Center](/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Center_(Sacramento) "Wells Fargo Center (Sacramento)") and [U.S. Bank Tower](/wiki/U.S._Bank_Tower_(Sacramento) "U.S. Bank Tower (Sacramento)"), two of the tallest buildings in the city, are located on Capitol Mall and are home to several major companies. The street is also home to major festivals such as the annual Farm to Fork Festival.

Sacramento's historic [Japantown](/wiki/Japantown#United_States "Japantown") once occupied much of today's Capitol Mall, spanning 4th street from K to P streets. The area suffered from the forced [eviction](/wiki/Internment_of_Japanese_Americans "Internment of Japanese Americans") of its Japanese residents during WW2 and never recovered, resulting in the remaining properties taken through eminent domain to create the grand promenade of today's [Capitol Mall](/wiki/Capitol_Mall#History "Capitol Mall"). The [Nisei Memorial Hall](/wiki/Nisei_VFW_Post_8985 "Nisei VFW Post 8985") at 4th and Q remains the last remaining property associated with Sacramento's former Japantown.[[41]](#cite_note-42)

##### Downtown Commons

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: Downtown Commons")]

One of the newest districts in the city is [Downtown Commons](/wiki/Downtown_Commons "Downtown Commons"). Formerly home to the Downtown Plaza shopping mall, the district opened in 2016 along with [Golden 1 Center](/wiki/Golden_1_Center "Golden 1 Center"). Downtown Commons, otherwise known as DOCO, is home to the Sawyer, a 16-story skyscraper with a 250-room hotel and 45 condominiums, a Macy's anchor store, an IMAX theater, and retail space with a variety of restaurants and shops.[[42]](#cite_note-43)

##### Downtown Sacramento

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: Downtown Sacramento")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Sacramento_aerial_overview.jpg/250px-Sacramento_aerial_overview.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sacramento_aerial_overview.jpg)

Aerial view of Sacramento, clearly showing the downtown/midtown grid and surrounding areas

See also: [Downtown Sacramento](/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento")

Downtown Sacramento is home to the [SAFE Credit Union Convention Center and Theater](/wiki/Sacramento_Convention_Center_Complex "Sacramento Convention Center Complex"), Sacramento City Hall, the [Sacramento Public Library](/wiki/Sacramento_Public_Library "Sacramento Public Library"), and [K Street](/wiki/K_Street_(Sacramento) "K Street (Sacramento)"), a historic street home to apartments, retail, and historical buildings. In addition, Downtown Sacramento is home to several hotels including the Citizen Hotel, housed in one of the first skyscrapers built in the city.[[43]](#cite_note-44)

##### East Sacramento

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: East Sacramento")]

See also: [East Sacramento](/wiki/East_Sacramento "East Sacramento")

East Sacramento is a neighborhood in between Midtown and Sacramento State. This neighborhood is well known for being home to McKinley Park and Rose Garden and the Fabulous Forties, home to some of the most expensive, largest, and architecturally unique homes in the city. East Sacramento was home to [Ronald Reagan](/wiki/Ronald_Reagan "Ronald Reagan") during his term as Governor of California and this neighborhood was prominently featured in Greta Gerwig's film [Lady Bird](/wiki/Lady_Bird_(film) "Lady Bird (film)").[[44]](#cite_note-45)

##### Historic Chinatown

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Historic Chinatown")]

The [Opium Wars](/wiki/Opium_Wars "Opium Wars") of the 1840s and 1850s, along with the California gold rush, brought many Chinese people to California. Most arrived at San Francisco, which was then the largest city in California and known as "Daai Fau" ([Chinese](/wiki/Chinese_language "Chinese language"): 大埠; [Jyutping](/wiki/Jyutping "Jyutping"): *daai6 fau6*; [Cantonese Yale](/wiki/Yale_romanization_of_Cantonese "Yale romanization of Cantonese"): *Daaihfauh*). Some eventually came to Sacramento, then the second-largest city in California and consequently called "Yee Fow" (Chinese: 二埠; Jyutping: *ji6 fau6*). Today the city is known as "萨克拉门托" ([pinyin](/wiki/Pinyin "Pinyin"): *Sàkèlāméntuō*) by mainland Chinese and as "沙加緬度" *Sāgāmíhndouh* and *Shājiāmiǎnduó* by Cantonese speakers and Taiwanese respectively.

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Sacramento_Chinatown_%E6%BA%AF%E6%BA%90%E5%A0%82_-_panoramio.jpg/250px-Sacramento_Chinatown_%E6%BA%AF%E6%BA%90%E5%A0%82_-_panoramio.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sacramento_Chinatown_%E6%BA%AF%E6%BA%90%E5%A0%82_-_panoramio.jpg)

Sacramento's historic Chinatown

Sacramento's [Chinatown](/wiki/Chinatowns_in_the_United_States "Chinatowns in the United States") was on "I" Street from Second to Sixth Streets, called the [China Slough](/wiki/China_Slough "China Slough"). At the time, this area of "I" Street was considered a health hazard because, lying within a levee zone, it was lower than other parts of the city, which were situated on higher land. Throughout Sacramento's Chinatown history, there were fires, acts of discrimination, and prejudicial legislation such as the [Chinese Exclusion Act](/wiki/Chinese_Exclusion_Act "Chinese Exclusion Act") that was not repealed until 1943. The mysterious fires were thought to be set off by those who resented the Chinese working class.[[45]](#cite_note-46) Ordinances on what was viable building material were set into place to try to get the Chinese to move out. Newspapers such as [The Sacramento Union](/wiki/The_Sacramento_Union "The Sacramento Union") wrote stories at the time that portrayed the Chinese in an unfavorable light to inspire ethnic discrimination and drive the Chinese away. While most of Sacramento's Chinatown has now been razed, a small Chinatown mall remains as well as a museum dedicated to the history of Sacramento's Chinatown.[[46]](#cite_note-47)[[47]](#cite_note-48)

##### Newton Booth Historic District

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Newton Booth Historic District")]

The Newton Booth Historic District, named for [Newton Booth](/wiki/Newton_Booth "Newton Booth"), is located on the southeast corner of Sacramento's original 1848 street grid.[[48]](#cite_note-cityofsacramento.org-Historic-District-Plans/Newton-Booth-49)[[49]](#cite_note-cityofsacramento-Historic-Register-074-50)[[50]](#cite_note-51)[[51]](#cite_note-sacbee-4484269-52)

##### Old Sacramento

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Old Sacramento")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Ebner%27s_Hotel_2011_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Ebner%27s_Hotel_2011_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ebner%27s_Hotel_2011_(cropped).jpg)

The historic [Ebner's Hotel](/wiki/Ebner%27s_Hotel "Ebner's Hotel"), built in 1856, in [Old Sacramento](/wiki/Old_Sacramento_State_Historic_Park "Old Sacramento State Historic Park")

The oldest part of the town besides [Sutter's Fort](/wiki/Sutter%27s_Fort "Sutter's Fort") is [Old Sacramento](/wiki/Old_Sacramento_State_Historic_Park "Old Sacramento State Historic Park"), which consists of cobbled streets and many historic buildings, several from the 1850s and 1860s. Buildings have been preserved, restored, or reconstructed, and the district is now a substantial tourist attraction, with rides on steam-powered historic trains and horse-drawn carriages.

##### Lavender Heights

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Lavender Heights")]

The Lavender District, formally designated as Lavender Heights in 2015, is central to Sacramento’s LGBTQ+ culture and community.[[52]](#cite_note-auto-53) It is home to the Gay & Lesbian Community Center, five LGBTQ+ nightclubs such as Badlands and [Faces](/wiki/Faces_(gay_club) "Faces (gay club)"), and numerous LGBTQ+-owned shops, galleries, and eateries.[[52]](#cite_note-auto-53)

##### Poverty Ridge Historic District

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Poverty Ridge Historic District")]

The Poverty Ridge Historic District is within Sacramento's original 1848 street grid and bounded to the west by 21st Street, to the north by S Street, to the east by 23rd Street, to the south by W Street and U.S. Route 50, and includes the block bounded by 20th Street, 21st Street, S Street, and T Street.[[53]](#cite_note-cityofsacramento.org-Historic-District-Plans/Poverty-Ridge-54)[[54]](#cite_note-newtonbooth-poverty-ridge-55)[[55]](#cite_note-56)

The Poverty Ridge Historic District was considered to be Sacramento's wealthiest neighborhood from 1868 to 1947.[[53]](#cite_note-cityofsacramento.org-Historic-District-Plans/Poverty-Ridge-54)[[56]](#cite_note-cityofsacramento-Historic-Register-076-57)

### Climate

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Climate")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/American_River_at_Sunrise_Park%2C_June_1974_%2826251615404%29.jpg/250px-American_River_at_Sunrise_Park%2C_June_1974_%2826251615404%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:American_River_at_Sunrise_Park,_June_1974_(26251615404).jpg)

The [American River](/wiki/American_River "American River") is popular for [kayaking](/wiki/Kayaking "Kayaking") and [recreational boating](/wiki/Recreational_boating "Recreational boating").

Sacramento has a [hot-summer Mediterranean climate](/wiki/Hot-summer_Mediterranean_climate "Hot-summer Mediterranean climate") ([Köppen](/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification") *Csa*), characterized by long, hot, dry summers and short, cool, rainy winters. Most of the annual precipitation generally occurs from November to April, though there may be a day or two of light rainfall in May or October. The normal annual mean temperature is 61.8 °F (16.6 °C), with the monthly daily average temperature ranging from 47.3 °F (8.5 °C) in December to 75.9 °F (24.4 °C) in July.[[57]](#cite_note-NCEI_Summary_of_Monthly_Normals_-_Airport_-_1991-2020-58) Summer heat is sometimes moderated by a sea breeze known as the "delta breeze" which comes through the [Sacramento–San Joaquin River Delta](/wiki/Sacramento%E2%80%93San_Joaquin_River_Delta "Sacramento–San Joaquin River Delta") from the [San Francisco Bay](/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay "San Francisco Bay"), and temperatures cool down sharply at night.

The foggiest months are December and January. [Tule fog](/wiki/Tule_fog "Tule fog") can be extremely dense, lowering visibility to less than 100 feet (30 m) and making driving conditions extremely hazardous. Chilling tule fog events have been known to last for several consecutive days or weeks. During Tule fog events, temperatures do not exceed 50 °F (10 °C).

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Farmers%27_market_Sacramento.jpg/250px-Farmers%27_market_Sacramento.jpg)](/wiki/File:Farmers%27_market_Sacramento.jpg)

A [market](/wiki/Farmer%27s_market "Farmer's market") at César Chávez Plaza

Snowfall is rare in Sacramento, which is only 25 ft (8 m) [above sea level](/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level "Above mean sea level"). In the downtown area, only three significant snow accumulations have occurred since 1900, the last one being in 1976.[[58]](#cite_note-59) During especially cold winter and spring storms, intense showers do occasionally produce a significant amount of hail, which can create hazardous driving conditions. Snowfall in the city often melts upon ground contact, with traceable amounts occurring in some years. Significant annual snow accumulations occur in the foothills 40 mi (64 km) east of the city, which had brief and traceable amounts of snowfall in January 2002, December 2009, and February 2011.[[59]](#cite_note-60)[[60]](#cite_note-61) The greatest snowfall ever recorded in Sacramento was 3 inches (7.6 cm) on January 5, 1888. On average, there are 76 days with a high of 90 °F (32 °C)+, and 14 days with a high of 100 °F (38 °C)+; On the other extreme, there are 8.5 days where the temperature remains below 50 °F (10 °C), and 15 freezing nights per year. Official temperature extremes range from 18 °F (−7.8 °C) on December 22, 1990, to 116 °F (46.7 °C) on September 6, 2022;[[61]](#cite_note-NOAA-62) a station around 5 mi (8.0 km) east-southeast of the city dipped to 17 °F (−8.3 °C) on December 11, 1932.[[62]](#cite_note-WRCC-63)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Sacramento_Skyline_%282%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Sacramento_Skyline_%282%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sacramento_Skyline_(2)_(cropped).jpg)

View of [Downtown Sacramento](/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento")

The average annual precipitation is 18.14 inches (461 mm). On average, precipitation falls on 58 days each year in Sacramento, and nearly all of this falls during the winter months. As in much of California, precipitation is highly variable from year to year, ranging from as little as 5.81 inches (148 mm) in 2013 to 33.44 inches (849 mm) in 1983.[[63]](#cite_note-64) Average January rainfall is 3.66 in (93 mm), and measurable precipitation is rare during the summer months. In February 1992, Sacramento had 16 consecutive days of rain, resulting in an accumulation of 6.41 in (163 mm) for the period. On rare occasions, monsoonal moisture surges from the Desert Southwest can bring upper-level moisture to the Sacramento region, leading to increased summer cloudiness, humidity, and even light showers and thunderstorms. Monsoon clouds do occur, usually during late June through early September. Sacramento is the second most flood-susceptible city in the United States after New Orleans.[[64]](#cite_note-65)

Sacramento has been noted as being the sunniest location on the planet for four months of the year, from June through September. It holds the distinction as the sunniest month, in terms of the percentage of possible sunshine, of anywhere in the world; July in Sacramento averages 14 hours and 12 minutes of sunshine per day, amounting to approximately 98% of possible sunshine.[[65]](#cite_note-66)

Since 2010, statewide [droughts in California](/wiki/Droughts_in_California "Droughts in California") have further strained Sacramento's [water security](/wiki/Water_security "Water security").[[66]](#cite_note-67)

In 2002, the Civil Rights Project at Harvard University conducted for *Time* magazine named Sacramento "America's Most Diverse City".[[76]](#cite_note-MostDiverseCity-TIME-78) The U.S. Census Bureau also groups Sacramento with other U.S. cities having a "high diversity" rating of the [diversity index](/wiki/Diversity_index "Diversity index").[[77]](#cite_note-79) Moreover, Sacramento is one of the most well-integrated U.S. cities, having a relatively high level of ethnic and racial heterogeneity within its neighborhoods.[[78]](#cite_note-80)

Chinese people are the largest Asian ethnic group in Sacramento, followed by Filipino, Indian, Vietnamese, Hmong and Japanese.[[79]](#cite_note-81)[[80]](#cite_note-82) Sacramento has the largest [Fijian American](/wiki/Fijian_American "Fijian American") community, including [Indo-Fijians](/wiki/Indo-Fijian "Indo-Fijian").[[81]](#cite_note-83)

### 2020

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: 2020")]

The [2020 United States census](/wiki/2020_United_States_census "2020 United States census") reported that Sacramento had a population of 524,943. The population density was 5,323.4 inhabitants per square mile (2,055.4/km2). The racial makeup of Sacramento was 34.8% [White](/wiki/White_Americans "White Americans"), 13.2% [African American](/wiki/African_Americans "African Americans"), 1.4% [Native American](/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States "Native Americans in the United States"), 19.9% [Asian](/wiki/Asian_Americans "Asian Americans"), 1.6% [Pacific Islander](/wiki/Pacific_Islander_Americans "Pacific Islander Americans"), 15.3% from [other races](/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census) "Race (United States Census)"), and 13.8% from two or more races. [Hispanic or Latino](/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans "Hispanic and Latino Americans") of any race were 28.8% of the population.[[87]](#cite_note-DP1-90)

The census reported that 96.7% of the population lived in households, 2.4% lived in non-institutionalized group quarters, and 0.9% were institutionalized.[[87]](#cite_note-DP1-90)

There were 192,560 households, out of which 30.7% included children under the age of 18, 37.9% were married-couple households, 8.9% were [cohabiting](/wiki/Cohabitation "Cohabitation") couple households, 32.0% had a female householder with no partner present, and 21.2% had a male householder with no partner present. 29.5% of households were one person, and 10.3% were one person aged 65 or older. The average household size was 2.64.[[87]](#cite_note-DP1-90) There were 116,436 [families](/wiki/Family_(U.S._Census) "Family (U.S. Census)") (60.5% of all households).[[88]](#cite_note-91)

The age distribution was 22.3% under the age of 18, 9.7% aged 18 to 24, 31.5% aged 25 to 44, 22.8% aged 45 to 64, and 13.8% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 35.4 years. For every 100 females, there were 95.2 males.[[87]](#cite_note-DP1-90)

There were 202,231 housing units at an average density of 2,050.8 units per square mile (791.8 units/km2), of which 192,560 (95.2%) were occupied. Of these, 49.2% were owner-occupied, and 50.8% were occupied by renters.[[87]](#cite_note-DP1-90)

In 2023, the US Census Bureau estimated that the median household income was $83,753, and the [per capita income](/wiki/Per_capita_income "Per capita income") was $42,300. About 10.3% of families and 14.4% of the population were below the poverty line.[[89]](#cite_note-92)

### 2010

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: 2010")]

The [2010 United States census](/wiki/2010_United_States_census "2010 United States census")[[90]](#cite_note-census2010-93) reported Sacramento had a population of 466,488. The population density was 4,660.0 inhabitants per square mile (1,799.2/km2).

There were 138,165 Hispanic or Latino residents of any race (26.9%); 22.6% of

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Sacramento_%285559878519%29.png/250px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Sacramento_%285559878519%29.png)](/wiki/File:Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Sacramento_(5559878519).png)

Map of racial distribution in [Greater Sacramento](/wiki/Greater_Sacramento "Greater Sacramento"), 2010 U.S. Census. Each dot is 25 people: **White**, **Black**, **Asian**, **Hispanic**, or **other**

the population was of Mexican heritage, 0.7% Puerto Rican, 0.5% Salvadoran, 0.2% Guatemalan, and 0.2% Nicaraguan.[[91]](#cite_note-94) [Non-Hispanic Whites](/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites "Non-Hispanic Whites") were 34.5% of the population in 2010,[[82]](#cite_note-census2-84) down from 71.4% in 1970.[[83]](#cite_note-census1-85)

The census reported 458,174 people (98.2% of the population) lived in households, 4,268 (0.9%) lived in non-institutionalized group quarters, and 4,046 (0.9%) were institutionalized. Demographics were not affected by the end of the [2000s United States housing bubble](/wiki/2000s_United_States_housing_bubble "2000s United States housing bubble") and the [2008 financial crisis](/wiki/2008_financial_crisis "2008 financial crisis").[[92]](#cite_note-95)[[93]](#cite_note-96)

There were 174,624 households, out of which 57,870 (33.1%) had children under the age of 18 living in them, 65,556 (37.5%) were [opposite-sex married couples](/wiki/Marriage "Marriage") living together, 27,640 (15.8%) had a female householder with no husband present, 10,534 (6.0%) had a male householder with no wife present. There were 13,234 (7.6%) [unmarried opposite-sex partnerships](/wiki/POSSLQ "POSSLQ"), and 2,498 (1.4%) [same-sex married couples or partnerships](/wiki/Domestic_partnership_in_California "Domestic partnership in California"). 53,342 households (30.5%) were made up of individuals, and 14,926 (8.5%) had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.62. There were 103,730 [families](/wiki/Family_(U.S._Census) "Family (U.S. Census)") (59.4% of all households); the average family size was 3.37.

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Sacramento%2C_CA_%E2%80%94_Westminster_Presbyterian_Church_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Sacramento%2C_CA_%E2%80%94_Westminster_Presbyterian_Church_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sacramento,_CA_%E2%80%94_Westminster_Presbyterian_Church_(cropped).jpg)

[Westminster Presbyterian Church](/wiki/Westminster_Presbyterian_Church_(Sacramento,_California) "Westminster Presbyterian Church (Sacramento, California)")

The age distribution of the city was as follows: 116,121 people (24.9%) were under the age of 18, 52,438 people (11.2%) aged 18 to 24, 139,093 people (29.8%) aged 25 to 44, 109,416 people (23.5%) aged 45 to 64, and 49,420 people (10.6%) who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 33.0 years. For every 100 females, there were 94.9 males. For every 100 females aged 18 and over, there were 92.2 males.

There were 190,911 housing units at an average density of 1,907.1 units per square mile (736.3 units/km2), of which 86,271 (49.4%) were owner-occupied, and 88,353 (50.6%) were occupied by renters. The homeowner vacancy rate was 2.8%; the rental vacancy rate was 8.3%. 231,593 people (49.6% of the population) lived in owner-occupied housing units and 226,581 people (48.6%) lived in rental housing units.

Sacramento has one of the highest [LGBT](/wiki/LGBT "LGBT") populations per capita, ranking seventh among major American cities, and third in California, behind San Francisco and slightly behind Oakland, with roughly 10% of the city's total population identifying themselves as gay, lesbian, transgender, or bisexual.[[94]](#cite_note-The_Seattle_Times-97) [Lavender Heights](/wiki/Lavender_Heights,_Sacramento,_California "Lavender Heights, Sacramento, California") is a hub for LGBTQ activities in the city[[95]](#cite_note-98)[[96]](#cite_note-99) and is a centrally located district in [Midtown Sacramento](/wiki/Midtown_Sacramento "Midtown Sacramento") centered within and around K & 20th streets.

## Economy

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Economy")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Californiastatecapitol.jpg/250px-Californiastatecapitol.jpg)](/wiki/File:Californiastatecapitol.jpg)

The [California State Capitol](/wiki/California_State_Capitol "California State Capitol") is the seat of the [Government of California](/wiki/Government_of_California "Government of California"), hosting the [Governor of California](/wiki/Governor_of_California "Governor of California") and the [California State Legislature](/wiki/California_State_Legislature "California State Legislature").

The [Sacramento metropolitan area](/wiki/Sacramento_metropolitan_area "Sacramento metropolitan area") is the fifth largest in California after the [Los Angeles metropolitan area](/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area "Los Angeles metropolitan area"), the [San Francisco Bay Area](/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area "San Francisco Bay Area"), the [Inland Empire](/wiki/Inland_Empire "Inland Empire"), and the [San Diego metropolitan area](/wiki/San_Diego_metropolitan_area "San Diego metropolitan area"), and is the [27th largest in the United States](/wiki/Table_of_United_States_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas "Table of United States Metropolitan Statistical Areas"). [[97]](#cite_note-100)[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*]

Sacramento's economy has historically been dominated by the state and federal government and is currently home to more than 120,000 public sector employees. However, in recent years Sacramento has seen a diversification in its local economy, with gains being made in healthcare,[[98]](#cite_note-101) manufacturing,[[99]](#cite_note-102) and technology.[[100]](#cite_note-103) [Adventist Health](/wiki/Adventist_Health "Adventist Health"), [Aerojet Rocketdyne](/wiki/Aerojet_Rocketdyne "Aerojet Rocketdyne"), [Blue Diamond Growers](/wiki/Blue_Diamond_Growers "Blue Diamond Growers"), [Golden 1 Credit Union](/wiki/Golden_1_Credit_Union "Golden 1 Credit Union"), [Kratos Defense & Security Solutions](/wiki/Kratos_Defense_%26_Security_Solutions "Kratos Defense & Security Solutions"), [Nugget Markets](/wiki/Nugget_Markets "Nugget Markets"), Powerschool, [Raley's Supermarkets](/wiki/Raley%27s_Supermarkets "Raley's Supermarkets"), Solidigm, [Sutter Health](/wiki/Sutter_Health "Sutter Health"), Teichert, [The McClatchy Company](/wiki/The_McClatchy_Company "The McClatchy Company"), and [VSP Vision Care](/wiki/VSP_Vision_Care "VSP Vision Care") are notable companies based in Sacramento and the surrounding metropolitan area. Other major companies that have operations in Sacramento include [Amazon](/wiki/Amazon_(company) "Amazon (company)"),[[101]](#cite_note-104) [Apple](/wiki/Apple_Inc "Apple Inc"), [Centene](/wiki/Centene "Centene"), [Hewlett-Packard](/wiki/Hewlett-Packard "Hewlett-Packard"), [Intel](/wiki/Intel "Intel"), [Oracle](/wiki/Oracle_Corporation "Oracle Corporation"), and [Siemens Mobility](/wiki/Siemens_Mobility "Siemens Mobility").[[102]](#cite_note-105)[[103]](#cite_note-106)[[104]](#cite_note-107)

The [Port of Sacramento](/wiki/Port_of_Sacramento "Port of Sacramento") has been plagued with operating losses in recent years and faces bankruptcy. This severe loss in business is due to the heavy competition from the [Port of Stockton](/wiki/Port_of_Stockton "Port of Stockton"), which has a larger facility and a deeper channel. As of 2006, the city of [West Sacramento](/wiki/West_Sacramento,_California "West Sacramento, California") took responsibility for the Port of Sacramento. During the [Vietnam War](/wiki/Vietnam_War "Vietnam War") era, the Port of Sacramento was the major terminus in the supply route for all military parts, hardware, and other cargo going to Southeast Asia.

## Culture

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Culture")]

### Museums

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Museums")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Crocker_Museum_entrance_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Crocker_Museum_entrance_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Crocker_Museum_entrance_(cropped).jpg)

The [Crocker Art Museum](/wiki/Crocker_Art_Museum "Crocker Art Museum") is the oldest public [art museum](/wiki/Art_museum "Art museum") in the [Western United States](/wiki/Western_United_States "Western United States") and has one of the largest public art collections in the country.

Sacramento is home to 32 museums, including several major museums. The [Crocker Art Museum](/wiki/Crocker_Art_Museum "Crocker Art Museum") is the oldest public [art museum](/wiki/Art_museum "Art museum") west of the [Mississippi River](/wiki/Mississippi_River "Mississippi River"). In 2010, the museum completed an expansion that tripled the museum's floor space to more than 145,000 square feet of exhibit space.

Also of interest is the [Governor's Mansion State Historic Park](/wiki/Governor%27s_Mansion_State_Historic_Park "Governor's Mansion State Historic Park"), a large Victorian Mansion that was home to 14 of California's Governors. The [Leland Stanford Mansion](/wiki/Leland_Stanford_Mansion "Leland Stanford Mansion"), which was completely restored in 2006, serves as the State's official address for diplomatic and business receptions. Guided public tours are available. [The California Museum for History, Women, and the Arts](/wiki/The_California_Museum_for_History,_Women,_and_the_Arts "The California Museum for History, Women, and the Arts"), home of the [California Hall of Fame](/wiki/California_Hall_of_Fame "California Hall of Fame"), is a cultural destination. The [California State Capitol](/wiki/California_State_Capitol "California State Capitol") is home to the [California State Capitol Museum](/wiki/California_State_Capitol_Museum "California State Capitol Museum") and offers free tours of the capitol's historic chambers and assembly rooms as well as a museum that is home to several historical artifacts.[[106]](#cite_note-109)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/California_Museum.jpg/250px-California_Museum.jpg)](/wiki/File:California_Museum.jpg)

[The California Museum](/wiki/The_California_Museum "The California Museum") is dedicated to the [history of California](/wiki/History_of_California "History of California") and also hosts the [California Hall of Fame](/wiki/California_Hall_of_Fame "California Hall of Fame").

The [California State Railroad Museum](/wiki/California_State_Railroad_Museum "California State Railroad Museum") in Old Sacramento has historical exhibits and live steam locomotives that patrons may ride. The [California Automobile Museum](/wiki/California_Automobile_Museum "California Automobile Museum"), just south of Old Sacramento, displays the automotive history and vehicles from 1880 to 2006 and is the oldest non-profit automotive museum in the West. [McClellan Air Force Base](/wiki/McClellan_Air_Force_Base "McClellan Air Force Base") is home to the [Aerospace Museum of California](/wiki/Aerospace_Museum_of_California "Aerospace Museum of California") where more than 40 civilian and military aircraft and 50 historical jet engines are displayed to the public. In addition, the [Sacramento History Museum](/wiki/Sacramento_History_Museum "Sacramento History Museum"), in the heart of Old Sacramento, focuses on the history of Sacramento from the region's pre-gold rush history through the present day. In 2021, the Museum of Science and Curiosity (MOSAC) opened in the restored historic power station building of Matsui Waterfront Park.

There is a Museum Day held in Sacramento every year when 26 museums in the greater Sacramento area offer free admission. The 2009 Sacramento Museum Day brought out more than 80,000 people, the largest number the event has gathered. Sacramento Museum Day is held every year on the first Saturday of February.

### Performing arts

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Performing arts")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Sacramento_Memorial_Auditorium_joins_the_LightSactoBlue_campaign.jpg/250px-Sacramento_Memorial_Auditorium_joins_the_LightSactoBlue_campaign.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sacramento_Memorial_Auditorium_joins_the_LightSactoBlue_campaign.jpg)

[Sacramento Memorial Auditorium](/wiki/Sacramento_Convention_Center_Complex "Sacramento Convention Center Complex") hosts the [Sacramento Ballet](/wiki/Sacramento_Ballet "Sacramento Ballet") and the [Sacramento Philharmonic Orchestra](/wiki/Sacramento_Philharmonic_Orchestra "Sacramento Philharmonic Orchestra").

The [Sacramento Ballet](/wiki/Sacramento_Ballet "Sacramento Ballet"), [Sacramento Philharmonic Orchestra](/wiki/Sacramento_Philharmonic_Orchestra "Sacramento Philharmonic Orchestra"), and the Sacramento Opera perform at the SAFE Credit Union Performing Arts Center (formerly known as the Community Center Theater).

There are several major theater venues in Sacramento. The [Sacramento Convention Center Complex](/wiki/Sacramento_Convention_Center_Complex "Sacramento Convention Center Complex") governs both the SAFE Credit Union Performing Arts Center and [Memorial Auditorium](/wiki/Memorial_Auditorium_(Sacramento) "Memorial Auditorium (Sacramento)"). The H Street Theatre Complex consists of the [Wells Fargo Pavilion](/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Pavilion "Wells Fargo Pavilion"), built in 2003 atop the old Music Circus tent foundations, the McClatchy Mainstage, and the Pollock Stage, originally built as a television studio and renovated at the same time the Pavilion was built. These smaller venues seat 300 and 90, offering a more intimate presentation than the 2300-seat Pavilion. The [Eagle Theatre](/wiki/Eagle_Theatre_(Sacramento,_California) "Eagle Theatre (Sacramento, California)") in Old Sacramento is a reconstruction of the oldest permanent theater in California and hosts several performances year-round.[[107]](#cite_note-110) The newest venue in the city, the Sophia Tsakopoulos Center for the Arts, consists of the 365-seat Sutter Theatre for Children and the Mainstage, seating 250.

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Wells_Fargo_Pavilion.jpg/250px-Wells_Fargo_Pavilion.jpg)](/wiki/File:Wells_Fargo_Pavilion.jpg)

The [Wells Fargo Pavilion](/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Pavilion "Wells Fargo Pavilion") hosts the [California Musical Theatre](/wiki/California_Musical_Theatre "California Musical Theatre") and the [Sacramento Theatre Company](/wiki/Sacramento_Theatre_Company "Sacramento Theatre Company").

Professional theatre is represented in Sacramento by several companies. [Broadway Sacramento](/wiki/Broadway_Sacramento "Broadway Sacramento") and its locally produced [summer stock theatre](/wiki/Summer_stock_theatre "Summer stock theatre"), [Broadway at Music Circus](/wiki/Broadway_at_Music_Circus "Broadway at Music Circus"), lures many directors, performers, and artists from New York and Los Angeles to work alongside a large local staff at the [Wells Fargo Pavilion](/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Pavilion "Wells Fargo Pavilion"). During the fall, winter, and spring seasons Broadway Sacramento brings bus and truck tours to the [SAFE Credit Union Performing Arts Center](/wiki/SAFE_Credit_Union_Performing_Arts_Center "SAFE Credit Union Performing Arts Center"). Resident at the H Street Theatre Complex for the remainder of the year (from September to May), the [Sacramento Theatre Company](/wiki/Sacramento_Theatre_Company "Sacramento Theatre Company") prepares to celebrate its 75th season, beginning in the Fall of 2019. In addition to a traditional regional theatre fare of classical plays and musicals, the Sacramento Theatre Company has a large School of the Arts with a variety of opportunities for arts education. The [B Street Theatre](/wiki/B_Street_Theatre "B Street Theatre"), having completed its 2018 move into the new Sofia Tsakopoulos Center for the Arts, continues its pursuit of producing smaller and more intimate professional works for families and children. Rounding out the professional companies is Capital Stage, which performed aboard the Delta King until the end of the 2010–2011 season and soon took up residence at its venue along the J-Street corridor.

The Sacramento area has one of the largest collections of community theatres in California. Some of these include the Thistle Dew Dessert Theatre and Playwrights Workshop, Davis Musical Theatre Co., El Dorado Musical Theatre, Runaway Stage Productions, River City Theatre Company, Flying Monkey Productions, The Actor's Theatre, KOLT Run Productions, Kookaburra Productions, Big Idea Theatre, Celebration Arts, Lambda Player, Light Opera Theatre of Sacramento, Synergy Stage and the historic Eagle Theatre. The [Sacramento Shakespeare Festival](/wiki/Sacramento_Shakespeare_Festival "Sacramento Shakespeare Festival") provides entertainment under the stars every summer in William Land Park. Many of these theatres compete annually for the Elly Awards overseen by The Sacramento Area Regional Theatre Alliance or SARTA.[[108]](#cite_note-111)

### Visual arts

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Visual arts")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Church_of_Scientology_Sacramento%2C_California.jpg/250px-Church_of_Scientology_Sacramento%2C_California.jpg)](/wiki/File:Church_of_Scientology_Sacramento,_California.jpg)

The [Spanish Colonial Revival style](/wiki/Spanish_Colonial_Revival_style "Spanish Colonial Revival style") Ramona Building, built in 1930

The Sacramento Metropolitan Arts Commission is an organization that was established as the Sacramento [arts council](/wiki/Arts_council "Arts council") in 1977 to provide several arts programs for the city. These include Art in Public Places, Arts Education, Grants, and Cultural Programs, Poet Laureate Programs, Arts Stabilization Programs and Other Resources, and opportunities.

Sacramento Second Saturday Art Walk is a program of local art galleries that stay open into the late evenings every second Saturday of each month.

Sacramento is also home to the [Wide Open Walls Festival](/wiki/Wide_Open_Walls_(Sacramento_Mural_Festival) "Wide Open Walls (Sacramento Mural Festival)") where artists from across the world have added more than 140 murals across the city since the festival's inception in 2016.[[109]](#cite_note-112)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Elks_and_Masons_4009_02.JPG/250px-Elks_and_Masons_4009_02.JPG)](/wiki/File:Elks_and_Masons_4009_02.JPG)

The [Sacramento Masonic Temple](/wiki/Sacramento_Masonic_Temple "Sacramento Masonic Temple")

Sacramento is home to one of California's oldest Latino cultural centers, the Latino Center of Art and Culture The Latino Center of Art and Culture was founded in the early '70s by activist Chicano students to combat racism and instill pride in the Chicano community. Known as La Raza Galeria it was home to artists like Ricardo Favela, José Montoya, and Esteban Villa who formed the Chicano artist collective, the Royal Chicano Air Force. The center is a community hub offering support to emerging Latino artists and producing live programming.[[110]](#cite_note-113)

### Music

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Music")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Tower_Theater_%2850216124686%29.jpg/250px-Tower_Theater_%2850216124686%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Tower_Theater_(50216124686).jpg)

The Tower Theatre, where [Tower Records](/wiki/Tower_Records "Tower Records") was founded

[Tower Records](/wiki/Tower_Records_(music_retailer) "Tower Records (music retailer)") was started and based in Sacramento until its closing.[[111]](#cite_note-CHanksBornRaised-Playmaker-114) Classical music is widely available. The [Sacramento Philharmonic Orchestra](/wiki/Sacramento_Philharmonic_Orchestra "Sacramento Philharmonic Orchestra"), the Sacramento Baroque Soloists, the Sacramento Choral Society & Orchestra, the [Sacramento Youth Symphony](/wiki/Sacramento_Youth_Symphony "Sacramento Youth Symphony"), the Sacramento Master Singers, the Sacramento Children's Chorus, and the Camellia Symphony each present a full season of concerts.

Each year, the city hosts the Sammies, the Sacramento Music Awards. Sacramento also has a reputation[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*] as a center for [Dixieland](/wiki/Dixieland "Dixieland") jazz, because of the [Sacramento Jazz Jubilee](/wiki/Sacramento_Jazz_Jubilee "Sacramento Jazz Jubilee") which was held every [Memorial Day](/wiki/Memorial_Day "Memorial Day") weekend until 2017. Events and performances are held in multiple locations throughout the city. Each year thousands of jazz fans from all over the world visit for this one weekend.

A growing number of rock, [hardcore](/wiki/Hardcore_punk "Hardcore punk"), and [metal](/wiki/Heavy_metal_music "Heavy metal music") bands hail from the Sacramento area, including [Tesla](/wiki/Tesla_(band) "Tesla (band)"), AS IS, [Deftones](/wiki/Deftones "Deftones"), [Papa Roach](/wiki/Papa_Roach "Papa Roach"), [Will Haven](/wiki/Will_Haven "Will Haven"), [Trash Talk](/wiki/Trash_Talk_(band) "Trash Talk (band)"),[[112]](#cite_note-115)[[113]](#cite_note-116)[[114]](#cite_note-117) [Dance Gavin Dance](/wiki/Dance_Gavin_Dance "Dance Gavin Dance"), [A Lot Like Birds](/wiki/A_Lot_Like_Birds "A Lot Like Birds"), [Far](/wiki/Far_(band) "Far (band)"), [CAKE](/wiki/Cake_(band) "Cake (band)"), [!!!](/wiki/!!! "!!!"), [Oleander](/wiki/Oleander_(band) "Oleander (band)") and [Steel Breeze](/wiki/Steel_Breeze "Steel Breeze"); plus some other famous musicians like record producer and recording artist [Charlie Peacock](/wiki/Charlie_Peacock "Charlie Peacock"), Duane Leinan, Bob Stubbs of [Social Distortion](/wiki/Social_Distortion "Social Distortion"), and Craig Chaquico of [Jefferson Starship](/wiki/Jefferson_Starship "Jefferson Starship").

Sacramento is home to several music festivals throughout the year. Since 2012, Sacramento hosts the four-day [Aftershock Festival](/wiki/Aftershock_Festival "Aftershock Festival") at [Discovery Park](/wiki/Discovery_Park_(Sacramento) "Discovery Park (Sacramento)") where acclaimed bands such as [Evanescence](/wiki/Evanescence "Evanescence"), [Kiss](/wiki/Kiss_(band) "Kiss (band)"), and [Muse](/wiki/Muse_(band) "Muse (band)") perform for up to 160,000 visitors. Other notable music festivals include the country-based GoldenSky Festival and the soul and R&B-based [Sol Blume](/wiki/Sol_Blume "Sol Blume") festival.[[115]](#cite_note-118)[[116]](#cite_note-119)

Scottish pop band [Middle of the Road](/wiki/Middle_of_the_Road_(band) "Middle of the Road (band)") sang kindly of Sacramento in their 1972 European hit song "[Sacramento](/wiki/Sacramento_(A_Wonderful_Town) "Sacramento (A Wonderful Town)")". [Experimental](/wiki/Experimental_music "Experimental music") groups such as [Hella](/wiki/Hella_(band) "Hella (band)"), [Death Grips](/wiki/Death_Grips "Death Grips"), and [Tera Melos](/wiki/Tera_Melos "Tera Melos") also come out of Sacramento.

Rappers [C-Bo](/wiki/C-Bo "C-Bo"), [Marvaless](/wiki/Marvaless "Marvaless"), [Lunasicc](/wiki/Lunasicc "Lunasicc"), [Mozzy](/wiki/Mozzy "Mozzy"), [Hobo Johnson](/wiki/Hobo_Johnson "Hobo Johnson"), and [Chuuwee](/wiki/Chuuwee "Chuuwee") are among those native to the area.

### Film

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Film")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/K_Street%2C_Downtown_Sacramento%2C_California_%2851030469438%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-K_Street%2C_Downtown_Sacramento%2C_California_%2851030469438%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:K_Street,_Downtown_Sacramento,_California_(51030469438)_(cropped).jpg)

The historic [Crest Theatre](/wiki/Crest_Theatre "Crest Theatre")

Sacramento is home to the [Sacramento French Film Festival](/wiki/Sacramento_French_Film_Festival "Sacramento French Film Festival"), a cultural event held every year in July that features U.S. premieres of French films and classic masterpieces of French cinema, and the Sacramento Japanese Film Festival,[[117]](#cite_note-120) also held in July. In addition, Sacramento is home to the Trash Film Orgy, a summer film festival celebrating the absurd, B-movies, horror, monster, and exploitation films.[[118]](#cite_note-121) Founded in 2007, the Sacramento Horror Film Festival showcases feature-length and short films as well as live musical and theatrical performances in the horror and macabre genres.[[119]](#cite_note-122)

Of note, Sacramento has been home to various actors, including [Eddie Murphy](/wiki/Eddie_Murphy "Eddie Murphy"), who resided in the Riverlake community of [Pocket-Greenhaven](/wiki/Pocket-Greenhaven "Pocket-Greenhaven") with his then-wife Nicole Mitchell Murphy, a fashion model and Sacramento native. It is also the home of director [Greta Gerwig](/wiki/Greta_Gerwig "Greta Gerwig"), whose solo directorial debut [*Lady Bird*](/wiki/Lady_Bird_(film) "Lady Bird (film)") is set in Sacramento.

### Cuisine

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Cuisine")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/The_Old_Tavern_%28Sacramento%2C_CA%29.jpg/250px-The_Old_Tavern_%28Sacramento%2C_CA%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_Old_Tavern_(Sacramento,_CA).jpg)

The [Old Tavern](/wiki/Old_Tavern_(Sacramento,_California) "Old Tavern (Sacramento, California)"), built in the 1850s

In 2012, Sacramento started the marketing campaign as "America's Farm-to-Fork Capital" due to Sacramento's many restaurants that source their food from the numerous surrounding farms[[120]](#cite_note-123) as well as the region's many certified farmers' markets.[[121]](#cite_note-124) Several notable farmers' market operate in the City of Sacramento, including:

* [Central Sacramento Sunday Certified Farmers' Market](https://alchemistcdc.org/central/) - one of the largest and longest-running agriculture-focused certified farmers' markets in California, it takes place every Sunday morning under the freeway overpass, across from [Southside Park](/wiki/Southside_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Southside Park, Sacramento, California") [[122]](#cite_note-125)
* [Midtown Farmers' Market](https://exploremidtown.org/midtown-markets/) - a large Saturday morning farmers' market that includes many hot food, packaged food, and craft vendors, the Midtown Farmers' Market was voted the #1 farmers' market in California and #3 farmers' market in the United States in 2025[[123]](#cite_note-126)
* [Florin Certified Farmers' Market](https://alchemistcdc.org/florin/) - located at the [Florin Light Rail Station](/wiki/Florin_station "Florin station") year-round on Thursday mornings, the Florin Certified Farmers' Market is among the top farmers' markets in the United States for [EBT](/wiki/Supplemental_Nutrition_Assistance_Program "Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program") usage.[[124]](#cite_note-127)

The city has an annual Farm-to-Fork festival that showcases various grocers, restaurants, and growers in the industry, and is the current host city for [Terra Madre](/wiki/Terra_Madre_Salone_del_Gusto "Terra Madre Salone del Gusto") Americas.[[125]](#cite_note-128) In 2012, one of the city's farm-to-fork restaurants [The Kitchen](/wiki/The_Kitchen_(California_restaurant) "The Kitchen (California restaurant)") was nominated for Outstanding Restaurant by the James Beard Foundation.[[126]](#cite_note-129) Sacramento is home to well-known cookbook authors, [Biba Caggiano](/wiki/Biba_Caggiano "Biba Caggiano") of Biba's Restaurant and Mai Pham of Lemongrass and Star Ginger.[[127]](#cite_note-130)

Sacramento is also known for its alcoholic beverage culture, with keystone events that include [Cal Expo](/wiki/Cal_Expo "Cal Expo")'s Grape and Gourmet, Sacramento Beer Week, and Sacramento Cocktail Week. Its growing beer scene is evident, with over 60 microbreweries in the region as of 2017.[[128]](#cite_note-131) Numerous beer festivals around the region highlight both local and visitor beers. In addition to festivals in Elk Grove,[[129]](#cite_note-132) Davis, Roseville, Placerville,[[130]](#cite_note-133) and Woodland,[[131]](#cite_note-134) Sacramento hosts the annual California Beer Craft Summit, an exposition dedicated to the art of brewing. The summit also hosts the largest beer festival on the West Coast, featuring over 160 breweries in downtown Sacramento.[[132]](#cite_note-135)

Sacramento's contemporary culture is also reflected in its coffee. An "underrated coffee city",[[133]](#cite_note-136) Sacramento has above-average marks for local coffee.[[134]](#cite_note-137)

## Sports

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Sports")]

Main article: [Sports in Sacramento, California](/wiki/Sports_in_Sacramento,_California "Sports in Sacramento, California")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/G1C_Interior.jpg/250px-G1C_Interior.jpg)](/wiki/File:G1C_Interior.jpg)

A [Sacramento Kings](/wiki/Sacramento_Kings "Sacramento Kings") game at [Golden 1 Center](/wiki/Golden_1_Center "Golden 1 Center") in [Downtown](/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento")

Sacramento is home of the [Sacramento Kings](/wiki/Sacramento_Kings "Sacramento Kings") of the [National Basketball Association](/wiki/National_Basketball_Association "National Basketball Association"). The Kings came to Sacramento from Kansas City in 1985. On January 21, 2013, a controlling interest in the Sacramento Kings was sold to hedge fund manager [Chris Hansen](/wiki/Chris_R._Hansen "Chris R. Hansen"), who intended to move the franchise to Seattle for the 2013–2014 NBA season and rename the team the [Seattle SuperSonics](/wiki/Seattle_SuperSonics "Seattle SuperSonics").[[135]](#cite_note-138) Sacramento Mayor [Kevin Johnson](/wiki/Kevin_Johnson_(basketball_player) "Kevin Johnson (basketball player)"), himself a former NBA basketball player, fought the move, forming an ownership group led by [Vivek Ranadive](/wiki/Vivek_Ranadive "Vivek Ranadive") to keep the Kings in Sacramento. On May 16, 2013, the NBA Board of Governors voted 22–8 to keep the Kings in Sacramento.[[136]](#cite_note-139)

[Sacramento Republic FC](/wiki/Sacramento_Republic_FC "Sacramento Republic FC") of [USL Championship](/wiki/USL_Championship "USL Championship") began play to in April 2014 at [Hughes Stadium](/wiki/Charles_C._Hughes_Stadium "Charles C. Hughes Stadium") before a sellout crowd of 20,231, setting a USL Pro regular-season single-game attendance record.[[137]](#cite_note-140)[[138]](#cite_note-141) They now play in Papa Murphy's Park. Republic FC won the [USL](/wiki/United_Soccer_League "United Soccer League") championship in their first season. In October 2019, Republic FC's [Major League Soccer](/wiki/Major_League_Soccer "Major League Soccer") expansion bid was approved; the team was expected to begin MLS play in the 2022 season,[[139]](#cite_note-142) until being delayed by COVID-19 to the 2023 season.[[140]](#cite_note-143) However, as of February 26, 2021, the bid is on indefinite hiatus.[[141]](#cite_note-144)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/City_Skyline_Raley_Field.JPG/250px-City_Skyline_Raley_Field.JPG)](/wiki/File:City_Skyline_Raley_Field.JPG)

View from [Sutter Health Park](/wiki/Sutter_Health_Park "Sutter Health Park"), home of the [Sacramento River Cats](/wiki/Sacramento_River_Cats "Sacramento River Cats") and the temporary home of the [Athletics](/wiki/Athletics_(baseball) "Athletics (baseball)").

In 2000, AAA minor league baseball returned to Sacramento with the [Sacramento River Cats](/wiki/Sacramento_River_Cats "Sacramento River Cats"), an affiliate of the [San Francisco Giants](/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants "San Francisco Giants") and formerly an affiliate of the [Oakland Athletics](/wiki/Oakland_Athletics "Oakland Athletics"). The River Cats play at [Sutter Health Park](/wiki/Sutter_Health_Park "Sutter Health Park"), in West Sacramento. The [Athletics](/wiki/Athletics_(baseball) "Athletics (baseball)") of [Major League Baseball](/wiki/Major_League_Baseball "Major League Baseball"), as part of their relocation from Oakland to [Las Vegas](/wiki/Las_Vegas "Las Vegas"), will temporarily play at Sutter Health Park from 2025 to 2027 (with an option for 2028), until their new stadium in Las Vegas is completed.[[142]](#cite_note-145)

The [Sacramento State Hornets](/wiki/Sacramento_State_Hornets_football "Sacramento State Hornets football") of the [NCAA Division I Football Championship Subdivision (FCS)](/wiki/NCAA_Division_I "NCAA Division I") play at [Hornet Stadium](/wiki/Hornet_Stadium_(Sacramento) "Hornet Stadium (Sacramento)") as part of the [Big Sky Conference](/wiki/Big_Sky_Conference "Big Sky Conference"). Since 1954, the Hornets have won seven conference titles and have participated in four playoff appearances and two bowl games.

Sacramento is the former home of two professional basketball teams. The [Sacramento Heatwave](/wiki/Sacramento_Heatwave "Sacramento Heatwave") of the [American Basketball Association](/wiki/American_Basketball_Association_(21st_century) "American Basketball Association (21st century)") previously played in the Sacramento area until 2013. Sacramento was also formerly home to the now-defunct [Sacramento Monarchs](/wiki/Sacramento_Monarchs "Sacramento Monarchs") of the [WNBA](/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association "Women's National Basketball Association"). The Monarchs were one of the eight founding members of the WNBA in 1997 and won the [WNBA Championship](/wiki/WNBA_Championship "WNBA Championship") in 2005, but folded in November 2009.

Sacramento has frequently hosted the [NCAA Men's Outdoor Track and Field Championship](/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Outdoor_Track_and_Field_Championship "NCAA Men's Outdoor Track and Field Championship") as well as the first and second rounds of the [NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship](/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship "NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship"). The California International Marathon (est. 1983) attracts a field of international elite runners who vie for a share of the $50,000 prize purse. The fast course is popular for runners seeking to achieve a Boston Marathon qualifying time and fitness runners.

## Parks and recreation

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Parks and recreation")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Capitol_Mall_Sacramento%2CCA.jpg/330px-Capitol_Mall_Sacramento%2CCA.jpg)](/wiki/File:Capitol_Mall_Sacramento,CA.jpg)

The [Capitol Mall](/wiki/Capitol_Mall "Capitol Mall") is a major monumental [parkway](/wiki/Parkway "Parkway") leading from [Tower Bridge](/wiki/Tower_Bridge_(Sacramento) "Tower Bridge (Sacramento)") to the [California Capitol](/wiki/California_State_Capitol "California State Capitol").

Sacramento boasts an extensive park system consisting of over 5,000 acres (2,023 ha) of parkland and recreation centers.[[143]](#cite_note-146) In its 2013 ParkScore ranking, [The Trust for Public Land](/wiki/Trust_for_Public_Land "Trust for Public Land") reported Sacramento was tied with San Francisco and [Boston](/wiki/Boston "Boston") for having the third-best park system among the 50 most populous U.S. cities.[[144]](#cite_note-147) ParkScore ranks city park systems by a formula that analyzes the city's median park size, park acres as percent of city area, the percent of residents within a half-mile of a park, spending of park services per resident, and the number of playgrounds per 10,000 residents.

The city features a collection of smaller parks in the downtown district, including Crocker Park, Roosevelt Park, Fremont Park, and Southside Park, and is home to basketball courts, playgrounds, and year-round farmers markets and local events. In addition, [Cesar Chavez Plaza](/wiki/Cesar_Chavez_Plaza "Cesar Chavez Plaza") is home to concerts in the summertime and is a well-known rallying spot for gatherings. In addition, surrounding the [California State Capitol](/wiki/California_State_Capitol "California State Capitol") is [Capitol Park](/wiki/Capitol_Park_(Sacramento) "Capitol Park (Sacramento)"), a 40 acres (16 ha) park consisting of more than 200 types of trees and 155 memorials. The most recent park constructed in Sacramento is the Hanami Line at [Robert Matsui](/wiki/Robert_Matsui "Robert Matsui") Waterfront Park, which is home to a line of [Cherry Blossoms](/wiki/Cherry_blossom "Cherry blossom") surrounding the park.[[145]](#cite_note-148) Popular parks outside the central core include [American River Parkway](/wiki/American_River_Parkway "American River Parkway") which spans 23 miles along the American River, William McKinley Park and Memorial Rose Garden, and [William Land Park](/wiki/William_Land_Park "William Land Park").

[William Land Park](/wiki/William_Land_Park "William Land Park") is home to several key attractions in the city. The [Sacramento Zoo](/wiki/Sacramento_Zoo "Sacramento Zoo") spans 14.3 acres (5.8 ha) and is home to more than 400 native and endangered animals around the world. The park is also home to Funderland, a small amusement park open from February to November consisting of 9 rides, and Fairytale Town, which sees more than 250,000 visitors each year. Once a year a [fire dancing](/wiki/Fire_dancing "Fire dancing") exhibition known as The Fire Spectacular is held in the park amphitheater. Groups from across Sacramento come to compete for the title of "Obsidian Fire". Jim Souza, the lead organizer of the event, came under controversy after local [H.O.A](/wiki/Homeowner_association "Homeowner association") members reported hooded individuals wearing black fire emblems strolling around the park. He denied having any connections and announced the event is still planned for fall 2024 of this year.[[146]](#cite_note-149)[[147]](#cite_note-150)[[148]](#cite_note-151)[[149]](#cite_note-152)

Sacramento is a hotbed for high school rugby. [Jesuit High School](/wiki/Jesuit_High_School_(Sacramento) "Jesuit High School (Sacramento)") is the recent defending national champion (winning five times in total). Their arch-rival school Christian Brothers came in second nationwide. Burbank, Del Campo, and Vacaville have also placed well in the national competition over the years. The Sacramento Valley High School Rugby Conference hosts the largest and arguably deepest preseason youth and high school rugby tournament in America.

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Monorail_and_rides_at_dusk_at_the_2012_California_State_Fair_held_in_Sacramento%2C_California_LCCN2013633011.tif/lossy-page1-250px-Monorail_and_rides_at_dusk_at_the_2012_California_State_Fair_held_in_Sacramento%2C_California_LCCN2013633011.tif.jpg)](/wiki/File:Monorail_and_rides_at_dusk_at_the_2012_California_State_Fair_held_in_Sacramento,_California_LCCN2013633011.tif)

The [California State Fair](/wiki/California_State_Fair "California State Fair") is held annually at the [California Exposition](/wiki/California_Exposition "California Exposition").

The [California State Fair](/wiki/California_State_Fair "California State Fair") is held in Sacramento each year at the end of the summer, ending on [Labor Day](/wiki/Labor_Day "Labor Day"). In 2010, the State Fair moved to July. More than one million people attended this fair in 2001. The [Jedediah Smith Memorial Trail](/wiki/Jedediah_Smith_Memorial_Trail "Jedediah Smith Memorial Trail") that runs between [Old Sacramento](/wiki/Old_Sacramento "Old Sacramento") and [Folsom Lake](/wiki/Folsom_Lake "Folsom Lake") grants access to the American River Parkway, a natural area that includes more than 5,000 acres (20 km2) of undeveloped land. It attracts cyclists and equestrians from across the state. Among other recreational options in Sacramento is Discovery Park, a 275-acre (1.1 km2) park studded with stands of mature trees and grasslands. This park is situated where the American River flows into the Sacramento River.

Since 1991, Capitol Casino has been open in downtown Sacramento and is home to several card games. Other notable casinos in the area include [Thunder Valley Casino Resort](/wiki/Thunder_Valley_Casino_Resort "Thunder Valley Casino Resort"), [Cache Creek Casino Resort](/wiki/Cache_Creek_Casino_Resort "Cache Creek Casino Resort"), and Hard Rock Hotel & Casino Sacramento at Fire Mountain.

In amateur sports, Sacramento claims many prominent Olympians such as [Mark Spitz](/wiki/Mark_Spitz "Mark Spitz"), [Debbie Meyer](/wiki/Debbie_Meyer "Debbie Meyer") (6-time gold medalist in US swimming), [Mike Burton](/wiki/Mike_Burton_(swimmer) "Mike Burton (swimmer)"), [Summer Sanders](/wiki/Summer_Sanders "Summer Sanders") (gold medalist in swimming, and trained in childhood by Debbie Meyer), [Jeff Float](/wiki/Jeff_Float "Jeff Float") (all swimming), and [Billy Mills](/wiki/Billy_Mills "Billy Mills") (track). Coach [Sherm Chavoor](/wiki/Sherm_Chavoor "Sherm Chavoor") founded Arden Hills Swim Club just east of the city and trained Burton, Spitz, and others.

## Government

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Government")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Sacramento_City_Hall_-_panoramio_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Sacramento_City_Hall_-_panoramio_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sacramento_City_Hall_-_panoramio_(cropped).jpg)

[Sacramento City Hall](/wiki/Sacramento_City_Hall "Sacramento City Hall") is the seat of the [Government of Sacramento](/wiki/Government_of_Sacramento "Government of Sacramento"), hosting the [Mayor of Sacramento](/wiki/Mayor_of_Sacramento "Mayor of Sacramento") and [Sacramento City Council](/wiki/Sacramento_City_Council "Sacramento City Council").

Sacramento is both the capital city of California and the [county seat](/wiki/County_seat "County seat") of [Sacramento County](/wiki/Sacramento_County "Sacramento County"). As such, it hosts both the [Californian government](/wiki/Government_of_California "Government of California") and the county administration, alongside the city government.

### City government

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: City government")]

Main article: [Government of Sacramento](/wiki/Government_of_Sacramento "Government of Sacramento")

The [Government of Sacramento](/wiki/Government_of_Sacramento,_California "Government of Sacramento, California") operates as a [charter city](/wiki/Charter_city "Charter city") (as opposed to a general law city) under the Charter of the City of Sacramento. The elected government is composed of the [Sacramento City Council](/wiki/Sacramento_City_Council "Sacramento City Council") with 8 city council districts and the [Mayor of Sacramento](/wiki/Mayor_of_Sacramento "Mayor of Sacramento"), which operates under a [council-manager government](/wiki/Council-manager_government "Council-manager government"). In addition, there are numerous departments and appointed officers such as the City Manager, [Sacramento Police Department](/wiki/Sacramento_Police_Department "Sacramento Police Department") (SPD), the [Sacramento Fire Department](/wiki/Sacramento_Fire_Department "Sacramento Fire Department") (SFD), City Clerk, City Attorney, and City Treasurer.

The current mayor is [Kevin McCarty](/wiki/Kevin_McCarty "Kevin McCarty") and the council members are Lisa Kaplan, Roger Dickinson, Karina Talamantes, Phil Pluckebaum, Caity Maple, Eric Guerra, Rick Jennings, and [Mai Vang](/wiki/Mai_Vang "Mai Vang").[[4]](#cite_note-cc-4) The City of Sacramento is part of [Sacramento County](/wiki/Sacramento_County,_California "Sacramento County, California"), for which the [government of Sacramento County](/wiki/Government_of_Sacramento_County,_California "Government of Sacramento County, California") is defined and authorized under the [California Constitution](/wiki/California_Constitution "California Constitution"), [California law](/wiki/California_law "California law"), and the Charter of the County of Sacramento.[[150]](#cite_note-153)

### California government

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: California government")]

Main article: [Government of California](/wiki/Government_of_California "Government of California")

As the [capital city](/wiki/Capital_city "Capital city") of [California](/wiki/California "California"), Sacramento is home to the [government of California](/wiki/Government_of_California "Government of California"). The California State Capitol is the seat of the [governor of California](/wiki/Governor_of_California "Governor of California") and the [California State Legislature](/wiki/California_State_Legislature "California State Legislature"), and the city is home to numerous [California state agencies](/wiki/List_of_California_state_agencies "List of California state agencies"). The [Supreme Court of California](/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_California "Supreme Court of California") is headquartered in San Francisco but maintains one of its two branch offices in Sacramento, where it shares a courtroom with the [Court of Appeal for the Third Appellate District](/wiki/California_Courts_of_Appeal "California Courts of Appeal").
