### State and federal representation

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: State and federal representation")]

In the [California State Senate](/wiki/California_State_Senate "California State Senate"), Sacramento is in the [8th Senate District](/wiki/California%27s_8th_State_Senatorial_district "California's 8th State Senatorial district"). In the [California State Assembly](/wiki/California_State_Assembly "California State Assembly") it is in the [6th Assembly District](/wiki/California%27s_6th_State_Assembly_district "California's 6th State Assembly district") and [10th Assembly District](/wiki/California%27s_10th_State_Assembly_district "California's 10th State Assembly district").

In the [United States House of Representatives](/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives "United States House of Representatives"), Sacramento is split between two districts. The northern half is in [California's 6th congressional district](/wiki/California%27s_6th_congressional_district "California's 6th congressional district"), represented by [Democrat](/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States) "Democratic Party (United States)") [Ami Bera](/wiki/Ami_Bera "Ami Bera").[[151]](#cite_note-154) The southern half is in [California's 7th congressional district](/wiki/California%27s_7th_congressional_district "California's 7th congressional district"), represented by [Democrat](/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States) "Democratic Party (United States)") [Doris Matsui](/wiki/Doris_Matsui "Doris Matsui").

## Education

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Education")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Aerial_view_of_UC_Davis_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Aerial_view_of_UC_Davis_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_UC_Davis_(cropped).jpg)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/UCDMCaerial.jpg/250px-UCDMCaerial.jpg)](/wiki/File:UCDMCaerial.jpg)

The main campus of the [University of California, Davis](/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis "University of California, Davis"), is in [Davis, California](/wiki/Davis,_California "Davis, California") (top), while the [UC Davis Medical Center](/wiki/UC_Davis_Medical_Center "UC Davis Medical Center") is in Sacramento (bottom).

### Higher education

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Higher education")]

See also: [California State University, Sacramento](/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento "California State University, Sacramento"); [University of California, Davis](/wiki/University_of_California,_Davis "University of California, Davis"); and [University of the Pacific (United States)](/wiki/University_of_the_Pacific_(United_States) "University of the Pacific (United States)")

The Sacramento area hosts a wide variety of higher educational opportunities. There are two major public universities, many private institutions, community colleges, vocational schools, and the McGeorge School of Law.

Sacramento is home to [Sacramento State (California State University, Sacramento)](/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento "California State University, Sacramento"), founded as Sacramento State College in 1947. In 2004, enrollment was 22,555 undergraduates and 5,417 graduate students in the university's eight colleges. The university's mascot is the hornet, and the school colors are green and gold. The 300-acre (1.2 km2) campus is along the American River Parkway a few miles east of downtown.

The [University of California](/wiki/University_of_California "University of California") has a campus, [UC Davis](/wiki/UC_Davis "UC Davis"), in nearby [Davis](/wiki/Davis,_California "Davis, California") and has a graduate center in downtown Sacramento. The [UC Davis Graduate School of Management](/wiki/UC_Davis_Graduate_School_of_Management "UC Davis Graduate School of Management") (GSM) is near the [UC Davis Medical Center](/wiki/UC_Davis_Medical_Center "UC Davis Medical Center") off Stockton Boulevard near Highway 50. Many students, about 400 out of 517, at the UC Davis GSM are working professionals and are completing their MBA part-time.[[152]](#cite_note-155) UC also maintains the University of California Sacramento Center (UCCS) for undergraduate and graduate studies.[[153]](#cite_note-156) The [UC Davis School of Medicine](/wiki/UC_Davis_School_of_Medicine "UC Davis School of Medicine") is at the [UC Davis Medical Center](/wiki/UC_Davis_Medical_Center "UC Davis Medical Center") between the neighborhoods of [Elmhurst](/wiki/Elmhurst,_Sacramento,_California "Elmhurst, Sacramento, California"), [Tahoe Park](/wiki/Tahoe_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Tahoe Park, Sacramento, California"), and Oak Park.

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Sac_State_Library_Quad.jpg/250px-Sac_State_Library_Quad.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sac_State_Library_Quad.jpg)

[Sacramento State University](/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento "California State University, Sacramento") is part of the [California State University](/wiki/California_State_University "California State University") system.

 [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Drexel_University%2C_Sacramento_campus.JPG/250px-Drexel_University%2C_Sacramento_campus.JPG)](/wiki/File:Drexel_University,_Sacramento_campus.JPG)

[Former Drexel University Sacramento](/wiki/Drexel_University_Sacramento "Drexel University Sacramento")

The [Los Rios Community College District](/wiki/Los_Rios_Community_College_District "Los Rios Community College District") consists of several [two-year colleges](/wiki/Community_college "Community college") in the Sacramento area—[American River College](/wiki/American_River_College "American River College"), [Cosumnes River College](/wiki/Cosumnes_River_College "Cosumnes River College"), [Sacramento City College](/wiki/Sacramento_City_College "Sacramento City College"), and [Folsom Lake College](/wiki/Folsom_Lake_College "Folsom Lake College"), plus a large number of outreach centers for those colleges. [Sierra College](/wiki/Sierra_College "Sierra College") is on the outskirts of Sacramento in Rocklin.

The [University of the Pacific](/wiki/University_of_the_Pacific_(United_States) "University of the Pacific (United States)") has its Sacramento Campus in the Oak Park neighborhood of Sacramento. The campus has long included [McGeorge School of Law](/wiki/McGeorge_School_of_Law "McGeorge School of Law") and in 2015 was expanded to become a comprehensive graduate and professional campus, including programs in analytics, business, education, health sciences, and public policy.[[154]](#cite_note-157) The [National University](/wiki/National_University_(California) "National University (California)") Sacramento regional campus offers bachelor's and master's degrees in business, education, health-care and teaching credential programs.

The [University of San Francisco](/wiki/University_of_San_Francisco "University of San Francisco") has one of its four regional campuses in Sacramento. At the undergraduate level, they offer degrees in Applied Economics, Information Systems, Organizational Behavior and Leadership, and Public Administration. At the graduate level, Master's programs are offered in Information Security and Assurance, Information Systems, Organization Development, Project Management, Public Administration, Nonprofit Administration, and Counseling.[[155]](#cite_note-158)

The private [University of Southern California](/wiki/University_of_Southern_California "University of Southern California") has an extension in downtown Sacramento, called the State Capital Center. The campus, taught by main campus professors, Sacramento-based professors, and practitioners in the State Capitol and state agencies, offers Master of Public Administration, Masters of Public Policy, and Master of Public Health degrees.[[156]](#cite_note-159)

[Epic Bible College](/wiki/Epic_Bible_College "Epic Bible College") and the [Professional School of Psychology](/wiki/Professional_School_of_Psychology "Professional School of Psychology") are also based in Sacramento. [Western Seminary](/wiki/Western_Seminary "Western Seminary") has one of its four campuses in Sacramento, which opened on the campus of Arcade Church in 1991. Western is an evangelical, Christian graduate school that provides theological training for students who hope to serve in a variety of ministry roles including pastors, marriage and family therapists, educators, missionaries, and lay leadership. The Sacramento campus offers four master's degrees and a variety of other graduate-level programs.[[157]](#cite_note-160)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/McGeorge_School_of_Law_logo.png/250px-McGeorge_School_of_Law_logo.png)](/wiki/File:McGeorge_School_of_Law_logo.png)

The [McGeorge School of Law](/wiki/McGeorge_School_of_Law "McGeorge School of Law") of the [University of the Pacific](/wiki/University_of_the_Pacific_(United_States) "University of the Pacific (United States)") is a [law school](/wiki/Law_school "Law school") in the [Oak Park neighborhood](/wiki/Oak_Park,_Sacramento,_California "Oak Park, Sacramento, California").

A satellite campus of [Alliant International University](/wiki/Alliant_International_University "Alliant International University") offers graduate and undergraduate programs of study.

[Carrington College](/wiki/Carrington_College_(US) "Carrington College (US)"), a for-profit institution, maintains a campus in Sacramento serving 2200 students. The school offers five programs in the healthcare professions.[[158]](#cite_note-161)

[The Art Institute of California – Sacramento](/wiki/The_Art_Institute_of_California_%E2%80%93_Sacramento "The Art Institute of California – Sacramento") was established in 2007 and is a branch of [The Art Institute of California – Los Angeles](/wiki/The_Art_Institute_of_California_%E2%80%93_Los_Angeles "The Art Institute of California – Los Angeles"). The school is focused on educating students in the field of commercial arts. The school offers both a Bachelor of Science and an Associate of Science degree, as well as diplomas in some areas of study. Some majors the school offers are Digital Film-making & Video Production, Culinary Management, Graphic Design, and Game Art & Design. The school has since been closed.

On J Street, there is the [Lincoln Law School of Sacramento](/wiki/Lincoln_Law_School_of_Sacramento "Lincoln Law School of Sacramento"), a private, evening-only law school program with a strong legal presence in the region.

The [Universal Technical Institute](/wiki/Universal_Technical_Institute "Universal Technical Institute") (UTI) is in Sacramento; it offers automotive programs in auto mechanics, auto body, and diesel.

### Primary and secondary education

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Primary and secondary education")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/C.K._McClatchy_High_School.jpg/250px-C.K._McClatchy_High_School.jpg)](/wiki/File:C.K._McClatchy_High_School.jpg)

The historic McClatchy High School

 [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Saint_Patrick_Academy_in_Sacramento_California_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Saint_Patrick_Academy_in_Sacramento_California_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Saint_Patrick_Academy_in_Sacramento_California_(cropped).jpg)

Saint Patrick Academy

 [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Sacramento_-_North_Sacramento_School_-_20211029085401_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Sacramento_-_North_Sacramento_School_-_20211029085401_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sacramento_-_North_Sacramento_School_-_20211029085401_(cropped).jpg)

North Sacramento School

The Sacramento area is served by various public school districts. They are: the [Sacramento City Unified School District](/wiki/Sacramento_City_Unified_School_District "Sacramento City Unified School District"), [Natomas Unified School District](/wiki/Natomas_Unified_School_District "Natomas Unified School District"), [San Juan Unified School District](/wiki/San_Juan_Unified_School_District "San Juan Unified School District"), [Twin Rivers Unified School District](/wiki/Twin_Rivers_Unified_School_District "Twin Rivers Unified School District"), [Elk Grove Unified School District](/wiki/Elk_Grove_Unified_School_District "Elk Grove Unified School District"), and [Robla Elementary School District](/wiki/Robla_Elementary_School_District "Robla Elementary School District"); secondary students in grades 7–12 in the Robla area are assigned to Twin Rivers USD.[[159]](#cite_note-SacCoSDMap2020-162) As of 2009, the area's schools employed 9,600 elementary school teachers (not including special education teachers),[[160]](#cite_note-163) and 7,410 middle school teachers (not including special education or vocational teachers).[[161]](#cite_note-164)

Almost all areas south of the American River are served by the Sacramento City Unified School District. The only exceptions are the Valley Hi/North Laguna and Florin areas served by the Elk Grove Unified School District.

Areas north of the American River are served by the remaining school districts. This area was not originally part of the City of Sacramento and as such is not served by Sacramento City Unified School District. North Sacramento outside of Natomas and Robla (for K-8) is served by the Twin Rivers Unified School District. The Robla area is served by the Robla School District for K-8 and by Twin Rivers for 9–12. The [Natomas](/wiki/Natomas,_Sacramento,_California "Natomas, Sacramento, California") region is served by the Natomas Unified School District. The Campus Commons area and the small portions of the Sierra Oaks neighborhood that fall into the city of Sacramento are served by the San Juan Unified School District.

While Roman Catholic institutions still dominate the independent school scene in the Sacramento area, in 1964, [Sacramento Country Day School](/wiki/Sacramento_Country_Day_School "Sacramento Country Day School") opened and offered Sacramento citizens an independent school affiliated with the California Association of Independent Schools. SCDS has grown to its present-day status as a learning community for students from pre-kindergarten through twelfth grade. Additionally, the suburb of [Fair Oaks](/wiki/Fair_Oaks,_California "Fair Oaks, California") hosts the expansive riverside campus of the [Sacramento Waldorf School](/wiki/Sacramento_Waldorf_School "Sacramento Waldorf School"), a [Steiner](/wiki/Waldorf_Education "Waldorf Education") school adjacent to the Rudolf Steiner College, and the largest Waldorf school in North America. Sacramento Waldorf School educates students from pre-K through 12th grade on a secluded, pastoral site that incorporates a large, functioning [biodynamic](/wiki/Biodynamic_agriculture "Biodynamic agriculture") farm.

Shalom School is the only Jewish day school in Sacramento; however, Brookefield School on property owned by Congregation B'nai Israel provides extracurricular Jewish education.

Capital Christian School is a preschool–12th grade private Christian school.[[162]](#cite_note-165) There is a small Bible college on campus offering associate degrees in Bible studies or theology. Sacramento Adventist Academy is another Christian school in Greater Sacramento. This is a preschool–12 institution, as well.

There is one Islamic school in Sacramento, Masjid Annur, founded in 1988.

The city also offers secular private schools, including [Merryhill School](/w/index.php?title=Merryhill_School&action=edit&redlink=1 "Merryhill School (page does not exist)") in Midtown.[[163]](#cite_note-166)[[164]](#cite_note-167)

### Public libraries

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: Public libraries")]

The [Sacramento Public Library](/wiki/Sacramento_Public_Library "Sacramento Public Library") system has 28 branches in the greater area.

## Transportation

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: Transportation")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/The_Tower_Bridge_2017-02-23_%2833055244176%29.jpg/250px-The_Tower_Bridge_2017-02-23_%2833055244176%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_Tower_Bridge_2017-02-23_(33055244176).jpg)

[Tower Bridge](/wiki/Tower_Bridge_(Sacramento) "Tower Bridge (Sacramento)") crosses over the [Sacramento River](/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River"), connecting Sacramento to [West Sacramento](/wiki/West_Sacramento,_California "West Sacramento, California").

Main article: [Transportation in the Sacramento metropolitan area](/wiki/Transportation_in_the_Sacramento_metropolitan_area "Transportation in the Sacramento metropolitan area")

A 2021 study by [Walk Score](/wiki/Walk_Score "Walk Score") ranked Sacramento the 49th most walkable of the 130 largest U.S. cities.[[165]](#cite_note-168)

### Roads

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Roads")]

Sacramento is a [control city](/wiki/Control_city "Control city") and the region is served by several highways and freeways. [Interstate 80](/wiki/Interstate_80_(California) "Interstate 80 (California)") (I-80) is the major east–west route, connecting Sacramento with San Francisco in the west, and [Reno](/wiki/Reno,_Nevada "Reno, Nevada") in the east. [Business 80](/wiki/Interstate_80_Business_(Sacramento,_California) "Interstate 80 Business (Sacramento, California)") (the Capital City Freeway) splits from I-80 in [West Sacramento](/wiki/West_Sacramento,_California "West Sacramento, California"), runs through Sacramento, and then rejoins its parent in the northwest portion of the city. [U.S. Highway 50](/wiki/U.S._Route_50_(California) "U.S. Route 50 (California)") also begins its eastern journey in West Sacramento, [co-signed](/wiki/Concurrency_(road) "Concurrency (road)") with Business 80, but then splits off and heads toward [South Lake Tahoe](/wiki/South_Lake_Tahoe,_California "South Lake Tahoe, California") as the El Dorado Freeway. A sign at the eastern terminus of US 50 in [Ocean City, Maryland](/wiki/Ocean_City,_Maryland "Ocean City, Maryland"), gives the distance to Sacramento as 3,073 miles (4,946 km).[[166]](#cite_note-169)

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Guy_West_Bridge_%285248634716%29_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Guy_West_Bridge_%285248634716%29_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Guy_West_Bridge_(5248634716)_(cropped).jpg)

[Guy West Bridge](/wiki/Guy_West_Bridge "Guy West Bridge") is a pedestrian and cyclist crossing over the [American River](/wiki/American_River "American River"), connecting [California State University, Sacramento](/wiki/California_State_University,_Sacramento "California State University, Sacramento") to the Campus Commons neighborhood.

[Interstate 5](/wiki/Interstate_5_(California) "Interstate 5 (California)") (I-5) runs through Sacramento, heads north up to [Redding](/wiki/Redding,_California "Redding, California"), and then heads south near the western edge of the [California Central Valley](/wiki/California_Central_Valley "California Central Valley") towards Los Angeles. [California State Highway 99](/wiki/California_State_Route_99 "California State Route 99") runs through Sacramento, heading closer to the eastern edge of the Central Valley, connecting to [Marysville](/wiki/Marysville,_California "Marysville, California") and [Yuba City](/wiki/Yuba_City,_California "Yuba City, California") in the north, and [Fresno](/wiki/Fresno "Fresno") and [Bakersfield](/wiki/Bakersfield "Bakersfield") in the south. [California State Highway 160](/wiki/California_State_Route_160 "California State Route 160") approaches the city after running along the [Sacramento River](/wiki/Sacramento_River "Sacramento River") from [Contra Costa County](/wiki/Contra_Costa_County,_California "Contra Costa County, California") in the south and then becomes a major city street in [Downtown Sacramento](/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento") before turning into the North Sacramento Freeway, going over the [American River](/wiki/American_River "American River") to Business 80.

Some Sacramento neighborhoods, such as Downtown Sacramento and [Midtown Sacramento](/wiki/Midtown_Sacramento "Midtown Sacramento") are very bicycle friendly as are many other communities in the region. As a result of litigation, Sacramento has undertaken to make all city facilities and sidewalks wheelchair accessible. In an effort to preserve its urban neighborhoods, Sacramento has constructed [traffic-calming](/wiki/Traffic_calming "Traffic calming") measures in many areas.

### Rail service

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: Rail service")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sacramento_Valley_Station_%28cropped2%29.JPG/250px-Sacramento_Valley_Station_%28cropped2%29.JPG)](/wiki/File:Sacramento_Valley_Station_(cropped2).JPG)

The historic [Sacramento Valley Rail Station](/wiki/Sacramento_Valley_Rail_Station "Sacramento Valley Rail Station"), utilized by [Amtrak California](/wiki/Amtrak_California "Amtrak California"), is a gateway to the [Sacramento Valley](/wiki/Sacramento_Valley "Sacramento Valley").

[Amtrak](/wiki/Amtrak "Amtrak") provides passenger rail service to the city of Sacramento. The [Sacramento Valley Rail Station](/wiki/Sacramento_Valley_Rail_Station "Sacramento Valley Rail Station") is on the corner of 5th and I streets near the historic Old Town Sacramento and underwent extensive renovations in 2007. The station serves as a [SacRT light rail](/wiki/SacRT_light_rail "SacRT light rail") terminus.

[Amtrak California](/wiki/Amtrak_California "Amtrak California") operates the *[Capitol Corridor](/wiki/Capitol_Corridor_(Amtrak) "Capitol Corridor (Amtrak)")*, a multiple-frequency service providing service from the capital city to its northeastern suburbs and the [San Francisco Bay Area](/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area "San Francisco Bay Area").[[167]](#cite_note-170)

Sacramento is the northern terminus of the [Amtrak California](/wiki/Amtrak_California "Amtrak California") *[Gold Runner](/wiki/Gold_Runner "Gold Runner")* route which provides direct multiple-frequency passenger rail service to California's Central Valley as far as [Bakersfield](/wiki/Bakersfield,_California "Bakersfield, California"); [Amtrak Thruway](/wiki/Amtrak_Thruway "Amtrak Thruway") connections are available from the trains at Bakersfield to [Southern California](/wiki/Southern_California "Southern California") and Southern [Nevada](/wiki/Nevada "Nevada"). An additional service under this banner is expected to be routed through Midtown in 2026.[[168]](#cite_note-ModestoACE-171)

Sacramento is a stop along Amtrak's *[Coast Starlight](/wiki/Coast_Starlight "Coast Starlight")* route which provides scenic service to [Seattle](/wiki/Seattle "Seattle") via [Klamath Falls](/wiki/Klamath_Falls,_Oregon "Klamath Falls, Oregon") and [Portland](/wiki/Portland,_Oregon "Portland, Oregon") to the north and Los Angeles via [San Luis Obispo](/wiki/San_Luis_Obispo,_California "San Luis Obispo, California") and [Santa Barbara](/wiki/Santa_Barbara,_California "Santa Barbara, California") to the south.

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Sacramento_WP_station%2C_October_2006.jpg/250px-Sacramento_WP_station%2C_October_2006.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sacramento_WP_station,_October_2006.jpg)

The historic [Sacramento Western Pacific station](/wiki/Sacramento_station_(Western_Pacific_Railroad) "Sacramento station (Western Pacific Railroad)") was served by the *[California Zephyr](/wiki/California_Zephyr_(1949%E2%80%931970) "California Zephyr (1949–1970)")* until 1970.

Amtrak's *[California Zephyr](/wiki/California_Zephyr "California Zephyr")* serves Sacramento daily and provides service to the east serving [Reno](/wiki/Reno,_Nevada "Reno, Nevada"), [Salt Lake](/wiki/Salt_Lake_City,_Utah "Salt Lake City, Utah"), [Denver](/wiki/Denver "Denver"), [Omaha](/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska "Omaha, Nebraska"), [Chicago](/wiki/Chicago "Chicago"), and intermediate cities.

[Sacramento Valley Station](/wiki/Sacramento_Valley_Station "Sacramento Valley Station") provides numerous Amtrak Thruway routes. One route serves the cities of [Marysville](/wiki/Marysville,_California "Marysville, California"), [Oroville](/wiki/Oroville,_California "Oroville, California"), [Chico](/wiki/Chico,_California "Chico, California"), [Corning](/wiki/Corning,_California "Corning, California"), [Red Bluff](/wiki/Red_Bluff,_California "Red Bluff, California"), and [Redding](/wiki/Redding,_California "Redding, California") with additional service to [Yreka](/wiki/Yreka,_California "Yreka, California") and even [Medford, Oregon](/wiki/Medford,_Oregon "Medford, Oregon"). A second serves the cities of [Roseville](/wiki/Roseville,_California "Roseville, California"), [Rocklin](/wiki/Rocklin,_California "Rocklin, California"), [Auburn](/wiki/Auburn,_California "Auburn, California"), [Colfax](/wiki/Colfax,_California "Colfax, California"), [Truckee](/wiki/Truckee,_California "Truckee, California"), Reno, and [Sparks](/wiki/Sparks,_Nevada "Sparks, Nevada"). The third and final Amtrak Thruway route serves [Placerville](/wiki/Placerville,_California "Placerville, California"), [Lake Tahoe](/wiki/Lake_Tahoe "Lake Tahoe"), [Stateline](/wiki/Stateline,_Nevada "Stateline, Nevada") Casinos, and [Carson City, Nevada](/wiki/Carson_City,_Nevada "Carson City, Nevada"). Each of these routes provides multiple frequencies each day.

Sacramento has the second busiest Amtrak station in California and the seventh busiest in the country.[[169]](#cite_note-172)

[Altamont Corridor Express](/wiki/Altamont_Corridor_Express "Altamont Corridor Express") [commuter rail](/wiki/Commuter_rail "Commuter rail") service is expected to be routed through Sacramento in 2026.[[168]](#cite_note-ModestoACE-171) This service will utilize the [Union Pacific](/wiki/Union_Pacific "Union Pacific")'s [Sacramento Subdivision](/wiki/Sacramento_Subdivision "Sacramento Subdivision"), the route of the original *California Zephyr*, where additional passenger capacity is available.[[170]](#cite_note-NewService-173)

Sacramento is expected to serve as the northern terminus of the [California High-Speed Rail](/wiki/California_High-Speed_Rail "California High-Speed Rail") system.

### Airport

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=48 "Edit section: Airport")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Sacramento_Airport%2C_Sacramento%2C_California_LCCN2013633188.tif/lossy-page1-250px-Sacramento_Airport%2C_Sacramento%2C_California_LCCN2013633188.tif.jpg)](/wiki/File:Sacramento_Airport,_Sacramento,_California_LCCN2013633188.tif)

[Sacramento International Airport](/wiki/Sacramento_International_Airport "Sacramento International Airport")

[Sacramento International Airport](/wiki/Sacramento_International_Airport "Sacramento International Airport") ([IATA](/wiki/IATA_airport_code "IATA airport code"): **SMF**, [ICAO](/wiki/ICAO_airport_code "ICAO airport code"): **KSMF**, [FAA](/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration "Federal Aviation Administration") [LID](/wiki/Location_identifier "Location identifier"): **SMF**) is a public [airport](/wiki/Airport "Airport") 10 miles (16 kilometers) northwest of downtown Sacramento, in [Sacramento County, California](/wiki/Sacramento_County,_California "Sacramento County, California"). [Southwest Airlines](/wiki/Southwest_Airlines "Southwest Airlines") is the dominant passenger airline with more than 104 daily flights to 25 cities across the US.[[171]](#cite_note-174) Other airlines include [Delta](/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines "Delta Air Lines"), [United](/wiki/United_Airlines "United Airlines"), [Spirit Airlines](/wiki/Spirit_Airlines "Spirit Airlines"), [American Airlines](/wiki/American_Airlines "American Airlines") and [Alaska Airlines](/wiki/Alaska_Airlines "Alaska Airlines"). The airport handles flights to and from various US destinations (including Hawaii) as well as Mexico, Canada and connecting flights to Europe, Asia, and South America, and served more than 13 million passengers in 2019.[[172]](#cite_note-175) The airport is well known for the 56-foot-long (17 m) red aluminum rabbit titled "Leap" by [Lawrence Argent](/wiki/Lawrence_Argent "Lawrence Argent") in Terminal B.[[173]](#cite_note-176)

[McClellan Airfield](/wiki/Sacramento_McClellan_Airport "Sacramento McClellan Airport") ([IATA](/wiki/IATA_airport_code "IATA airport code"): **MCC**, [ICAO](/wiki/ICAO_airport_code "ICAO airport code"): **KMCC**, [FAA](/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration "Federal Aviation Administration") [LID](/wiki/Location_identifier "Location identifier"): **MCC**) is a privately owned, public-use [airport](/wiki/Airport "Airport") that is mainly used for general aviation. It is located in the unincorporated area of [McClellan Park, California](/wiki/McClellan_Park,_California "McClellan Park, California"), six miles (9.7 km; 5.2 nmi) northeast of the [central business district](/wiki/Central_business_district "Central business district") of Sacramento. The airport is on the former site of **[McClellan Air Force Base](/wiki/McClellan_Air_Force_Base "McClellan Air Force Base")**, and was transferred to Sacramento County in 2000. The airport is a public-use facility which operates as an uncontrolled airfield in what the FAA designates as Class "E" Airspace.

### Transit

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=49 "Edit section: Transit")]

[![A blue light rail train pulling into Mather Field/Mills station.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/LightrailMather.jpg/250px-LightrailMather.jpg)](/wiki/File:LightrailMather.jpg)

The [SacRT lightrail](/wiki/SacRT_light_rail "SacRT light rail") pulling into [Mather Field/Mills station](/wiki/Mather_Field/Mills_station "Mather Field/Mills station").

The city and its suburbs are served by [Sacramento Regional Transit District](/wiki/Sacramento_Regional_Transit_District "Sacramento Regional Transit District"), which ranks as [the eleventh busiest in the United States](/wiki/List_of_United_States_Light_Rail_systems_by_ridership "List of United States Light Rail systems by ridership"). Sac RT is a bus and light-rail system, with 274 buses and 76 light-rail vehicles providing service for 58,200 daily passengers. The three light-rail lines (Blue, Gold, & Green) is a 42.9 mi (69.0 km) system with 54 stations. The Gold Line was extended east as far as the city of [Folsom](/wiki/Folsom,_California "Folsom, California"), and more recently the Blue Line was extended south from Meadowview Rd to [Cosumnes River College](/wiki/Cosumnes_River_College "Cosumnes River College"). Sacramento's light rail system goes to the [Sacramento Valley Rail Station](/wiki/Sacramento_Valley_Rail_Station "Sacramento Valley Rail Station"), [Cosumnes River College Station](/wiki/Cosumnes_River_College_(Sacramento_RT) "Cosumnes River College (Sacramento RT)") in south Sacramento, and north to Watt/I-80 where [I-80](/wiki/I-80 "I-80") and Business 80 meeting. The light-rail Blue & Gold Lines have 15-minute weekday headways and 30-minute weekday evening and weekend/holiday headways; the Green Line has 30-minute weekday headways and no weekend service. Route 142 is an express bus line to/from [downtown](/wiki/Downtown_Sacramento "Downtown Sacramento") to Sacramento International Airport.[[174]](#cite_note-Bus_Route_Webpage-177) There are expansion plans to extend the Green Line to the [airport](/wiki/Sacramento_International_Airport "Sacramento International Airport") and the Blue Line to the City of [Roseville](/wiki/Roseville,_California "Roseville, California") through the City of [Citrus Heights](/wiki/Citrus_Heights,_California "Citrus Heights, California"). [Yolobus](/wiki/Yolobus "Yolobus") provides bus service to [West Sacramento](/wiki/West_Sacramento,_California "West Sacramento, California") and [Yolo County](/wiki/Yolo_County,_California "Yolo County, California").

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Delta_King.JPG/250px-Delta_King.JPG)](/wiki/File:Delta_King.JPG)

[Old Sacramento](/wiki/Old_Sacramento "Old Sacramento")'s riverfront docks

[Greyhound Lines](/wiki/Greyhound_Lines "Greyhound Lines") provides intercity bus service to Portland, Reno, Los Angeles, and San Francisco from its new station along Richards Boulevard. Intercity bus service to San Francisco and [Sparks, Nevada](/wiki/Sparks,_Nevada "Sparks, Nevada") is offered by [Megabus](/wiki/Megabus_(North_America) "Megabus (North America)").[[175]](#cite_note-178)

[Bicycling](/wiki/Bicycling "Bicycling") is an increasingly popular transportation mode in Sacramento, which enjoys a mild climate and flat terrain. Bicycling is especially common in the older neighborhoods of Sacramento's center, such as Alkali Flat, [Midtown](/wiki/Midtown_Sacramento "Midtown Sacramento"), McKinley Park, [Land Park](/wiki/Land_Park "Land Park"), and [East Sacramento](/wiki/East_Sacramento "East Sacramento"). Many employees who work downtown commute by bicycle from suburban communities on a dedicated bicycle path on the [American River Parkway](/wiki/American_River_Parkway "American River Parkway"). Sacramento was designated as a Silver Level Bicycle Friendly Community by the [League of American Bicyclists](/wiki/League_of_American_Bicyclists "League of American Bicyclists") in September 2006. The advocacy organization [Sacramento Area Bicycle Advocates](/wiki/Sacramento_Area_Bicycle_Advocates "Sacramento Area Bicycle Advocates") co-sponsors the Sacramento Area Council of Governments' May is Bike Month campaign. Rideshare companies such as [Lime](/wiki/Lime_(transportation_company) "Lime (transportation company)"), [Bird](/wiki/Bird_(transportation_company) "Bird (transportation company)"), and [Helbiz](/wiki/Helbiz "Helbiz") have introduced up to 4,000 electric-powered scooters and bikes in Downtown Sacramento for residents to rent as a faster and alternative way to get around the city. Sacramento ranks second worldwide in ride sharable, with ridership totaling 1 million riders in 8 months.[[176]](#cite_note-179)[[177]](#cite_note-180)

There is a commuter bus service from Yolo County on [Yolobus](/wiki/Yolobus "Yolobus"), from Solano County on [FAST](/wiki/Fairfield_and_Suisun_Transit "Fairfield and Suisun Transit"), on two bus lines from [Yuba County](/wiki/Yuba_County,_California "Yuba County, California")'s [Yuba Sutter Transit](/wiki/Yuba_Sutter_Transit "Yuba Sutter Transit"),[[178]](#cite_note-181) from [Amador](/wiki/Amador_County,_California "Amador County, California") Transit's Sacramento Line,[[179]](#cite_note-182) on [Placer County Transit](/wiki/Placer_County_Transit "Placer County Transit")'s Auburn to Light Rail Line,[[180]](#cite_note-183) and from [San Joaquin County](/wiki/San_Joaquin_County,_California "San Joaquin County, California") on several [SMART](/wiki/San_Joaquin_Regional_Transit_District "San Joaquin Regional Transit District") bus lines.

## International relations

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=51 "Edit section: International relations")]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Stanford_Mansion_%28Sacramento%2C_California%29.jpg/250px-Stanford_Mansion_%28Sacramento%2C_California%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Stanford_Mansion_(Sacramento,_California).jpg)

[Stanford Mansion](/wiki/Leland_Stanford_Mansion "Leland Stanford Mansion") is the official reception center for the [Californian government](/wiki/Government_of_California "Government of California") and one of the workplaces of the [Governor of California](/wiki/Governor_of_California "Governor of California").

As of 2023, the City of Sacramento has 14 [sister cities](/wiki/Sister_city "Sister city"). They are:[[181]](#cite_note-184)

| Moldova | [Chişinău](/wiki/Chi%C5%9Fin%C4%83u "Chişinău")[[182]](#cite_note-Chișinău_twinnings-185) | December 12, 1989 |
| New Zealand | [Hamilton](/wiki/Hamilton,_New_Zealand "Hamilton, New Zealand") | December 6, 1988 |
| China | [Jinan](/wiki/Jinan "Jinan"), [Shandong](/wiki/Shandong "Shandong") | October 16, 1984 |
| Switzerland | [Liestal](/wiki/Liestal "Liestal") | March 21, 1989 |

## Explanatory notes

[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Sacramento,_California&action=edit&section=53 "Edit section: Explanatory notes")]

1. **[^](#cite_ref-11)** 

   * [American English](/wiki/American_English "American English"): [/ˌsækrəˈmɛntoʊ/](/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Help:IPA/English") [ⓘ](/wiki/File:LL-Q1860_(eng)-Flame,_not_lame-Sacramento,_California.wav "File:LL-Q1860 (eng)-Flame, not lame-Sacramento, California.wav") [*SAK-rə-MEN-toh*](/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key "Help:Pronunciation respelling key"),[[9]](#cite_note-9) locally [/-ˈmɛnoʊ/](/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Help:IPA/English") [*-⁠MEN-oh*](/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key "Help:Pronunciation respelling key");[[10]](#cite_note-10)
   * Spanish: [[sakɾaˈmento]](/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish "Help:IPA/Spanish"), lit. 'sacrament'
2. **[^](#cite_ref-69)** Official records for Sacramento were kept exclusively at the airport since 10 November 1941.[[67]](#cite_note-68)
3. ^ [***a***](#cite_ref-fifteen_86-0) [***b***](#cite_ref-fifteen_86-1) From 15% sample

# Visit the State Capitol

## [Resources](/resources "Resources")

## WAS User Menu

At the State Capitol, the past, present and future of California interact with equal force. The building serves as both a museum and the state’s working seat of government. Visitors to the Capitol can at once experience California’s rich history and witness the making of history through the modern lawmaking process.

## California Capitols

Shortly after the end of Mexican rule, Californians began to clamor for statehood. In 1849, a constitutional convention met at Colton Hall in Monterey and proposed a constitution, subsequently ratified by the people, which named San Jose as the first capital.

In December 1849, the first Legislature convened in a two-story adobe hotel in San Jose. The city was composed of little more than huts, tents and clapboard buildings, and the general discomfort did little to endear the city to the legislators.In 1851 a generous offer from General Vallejo induced the legislators to move the capital to Vallejo where a frame building had been erected for their use. Since housing was virtually nonexistent, many of the Members managed to secure lodging on the steamer Empire, which remained moored at a wharf during the session.

![](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAAAACH5BAEKAAEALAAAAAABAAEAAAICTAEAOw==)

Confusion and inconvenience again brought stormy cries for relocation. After convening in Vallejo in 1852, the Legislature moved to Sacramento to finish the legislative session. In 1853, the Legislature returned to Vallejo only to find conditions as inhospitable as before. To an exasperated membership, an offer from the community of Benicia for the use of its new city hall proved irresistible, and a bill was passed moving the seat of government to that city, where the legislative session finished.

While the legislative quarters were adequate, it became increasingly evident that Benicia itself was too small to serve as the capital city. With this in mind, the Legislature determined that Sacramento would be the state’s capital and moved from Benicia in February 1854. Sacramento offered its courthouse for immediate use and a building site for the permanent Capitol. Shortly after the close of the Session of 1854, the courthouse was razed by fire, but a new one was completed in time for the next session.

The new courthouse continued to serve as the home of the Legislature until 1869. This tenure was interrupted only once; during the winter of 1861–62 a severe flood prompted removal of the Legislature to the Exchange Building in San Francisco. Construction on the permanent Capitol was begun in 1860, and, though not completed until 1874, the Legislature was able to occupy its Chambers in 1869. Except for a major “modernization” in 1908, the Capitol remained virtually unchanged until 1949 when additional space requirements resulted in the construction of the Capitol Annex. Completed in 1951, the Annex attaches to the east side of the old Capitol and houses legislative offices, committee rooms and the Governor’s offices.

In 1976, a total reconstruction of the building was undertaken to strengthen and reinforce the weakening structure. This monumental project was completed in January 1982, and the old Capitol, restored to its turn-of-the-century decor, was again occupied by the Legislature and opened to the public.

During session, wait times for elevators may be extended. Please plan your visit accordingly. | Front entrance is wheelchair accessible. |

The North (L Street) and South (N Street) entrances have wheelchair ramps.

Sidewalks leading to the Capitol are wheelchair accessible.

Elevators accessible to the general public are located at the back of the building after passing through security.

During session, wait times for elevators may be extended. Please plan your visit accordingly.

![](https://californiathroughmylens.com/wp-content/uploads/2012/03/state-capitol-of-california.jpg)

# California’s State Capitol in Sacramento

The Capitol Building of California, in the town of Sacramento, is a beautiful example of Roman architecture, complete with a portico opening that leads to a central dome. This type of design can be found on many of the capitols around the county, but of course, most notably in Washington DC. A visit to this fantastic building is like a step back in time to when design and architecture were unique and extravagant. Add to that the beautiful interior, and the acres of green land you can wander through surrounding it, and you have the recipe for a great half-day adventure.

### **Details**

* Free
* Hours: Weekdays: 8 AM – 5 PM, Weekends: 9 AM – 5 PM
* Tours hourly
* Metered street parking
* *Written from my visit in 2018*

### History

*“The immigration of thousands of “Forty-niners” in search of gold prompted California’s admission as the 31st state into the Union in 1850, thus creating the need for a state capital. California did not have a permanent seat of government until 1860. Cities vied for the opportunity to house the state capital for the power, prestige, and economic benefit that accompanied it. Four capitol buildings existed in other cities before Sacramento became the permanent site. Even after Sacramento became the permanent seat of California’s government in 1854, there were several unsuccessful efforts to relocate the Capitol to Oakland (1858-59), San Jose (1875-78, 1893, 1903), Berkeley (1907), and Monterey (1933-41).  After deciding on Sacramento in 1854, $500,000 was appropriated to build a new capital. Construction on the present-day Capitol began in 1860, and the building has endured for more than 125 years after its completion in 1874.”*

### The Exterior

Even if you come when the inside is closed, the outside of the building is always open, so you can come by to take pictures without going inside. I was more of a fan of Capitol Park on the outside of the capitol than the inside as it had a lot of beautiful trees and plant life representing the different species you can see around the state of California. It even has a signed walk that shows you all of the various plant varieties that make up Capitol Park as well as memorials to different events in California’s history. You can take an [online tour](http://capitolmuseum.ca.gov/VirtualTour.aspx?Content1=1416&Content2=1420&Content3=542) of some of the best attractions if you are too far away to visit for yourself.

**The Interior**

If you come when the museum is open, you can experience and see a lot of exciting pieces of California’s history, including the senate. You can also see the restored historical offices of the Secretary of State, Treasurer, and the Governor.

The Senate and the House of Representatives chambers are both amazing rooms that you must see when you visit. They can be accessed by the third-floor walkway which takes you to a seating area for the general public that looks down on the representatives. Nothing was happening when I was there, but it was still awesome to see.

Also of note, on the third floor is the paintings of all the governors of California. Of course, it was pretty funny to see Arnold’s painting sitting here as well, and I couldn’t help but snap a photo.

Lastly, make sure you go by the fantastic rotunda that is directly across the building from where you enter. This room is stunning and reminded me of the architecture that you would see in a famous European building.

All in all, the Capitol Building in Sacramento is a fantastic spot to explore. I would recommend you visit it when it is open so that you can see some of the interior beauty, but even if you just by the outside, you will still love seeing this magnificent building. Let me know if you have been in the comments.

 

1315 10th St Sacramento, CA 95814
